COURSE: The Art of Astral Projection
AUTHOR: Jade Shaw
====================

Preparation

========================================

Preparation 1: What Is Astral Projection?
--------------------
<v ->Hello Mindvalley students.</v> Welcome to your quest on spiritual integration through the Art of Astral Projection. So before we start our journey, let's look at what Astral Projection is and what some of the benefits of this practice can be so that you can not only understand it but be fully immersed in this practice and get the maximum results. Astral Projection is a self-initiated out-of-body experience, usually associated with the astral planes. During an out-of-body experience, our self-awareness, so where we perceive ourselves to be in time and space, isn't operating in the same place as the physical body. In other words, we appear to experience the world from outside of it. So if I were to have an out-of-body experience right this second, it would be a little bit like I shift out of my physical body, and I'm able to turn around and look at myself, sitting there. It's that real. So during a full-blown OBE, out-of-body experience, there's a visceral feeling of exiting, such as floating or phasing out of the body. Sometimes we appear in a second body, often experienced as energy or light. Imagine slipping out of your skin like a jacket or stretching away from the body like caramel or dissolving out like a puff of smoke. One time I swung both my legs out of my body, sat up, and walked away from it. After leaving the body, we appear to travel in other realms of reality, encountering beings and places that seem real. Sounds pretty far out, right? So let's look at what might be happening when this occurs. Shamans enter trance, Buddhists meditate, and Dervishes whirl, all to connect to deeper parts of themselves and the wider world. Science calls it Polyphasic Perception. They call it being human. These alternative ways of knowing are found in over 90% of the world's cultures and are not considered strange at all. So why in the modern world, are these experiences written off as woo-woo? Because we've lost this perceptual diversity, different ways of gaining knowledge. We get flashes of insight through epiphanies and creativity and meditation. But for the most part, we see through one lens, and it's blinding. Neuroscience and psychology is now beginning to catch up to the health benefits of non-ordinary states of consciousness. And the good news is that these states are not limited to the wise man or medicine woman. In fact, you have probably experienced one without even knowing. Chanting football fans, nature dwellers, and clubbing ravers can all enter various altered states. This is due to the way these events naturally alter our brainwaves via song and dance, deep presence, and feelings of awe. Yet, whilst you can simply rest in an altered state, like the time you daydreamed at school or did your meditation, we can also use it to channel focus, explore the mind, or even develop extra sensory perception. This is because an altered state is a bit like getting into a car. There are different types, and we can use the gears to direct the destination. However, most people don't know how to drive so they just sit there. Until now. Techies are leveling up their focus by micro-dosing in Silicon Valley. The Navy SEALS are hacking flow states for athletic performance, and stressed-out office workers are using mindfulness for better health. Ordinary people are discovering fields of super-human awareness. Astral Projection is one of them. In this quest, we are going to harness totally natural altered states of consciousness to self-initiate an out of body experience for the purpose of self-transformation. This esoteric term, Astral Projection, alludes to the spirit or soul leaving the body, as believed in some spiritual traditions. When you hear stories of people floating out of their bodies, you can certainly see why. Astral Projection is not some new age invention; it has a long history within cultures all around the world. One cross-cultural study of 488 societies found that 89% of them made reference to out-of-body states of consciousness, and descriptions of what appear to be like astral travel experiences featured in spiritual texts of all the world's major religions. Within ancient Hinduism, Astral Projection is one of the super power Siddhis, considered achievable by advanced yoga practitioners. And modern masters, such as Paramahansa Yogananda vouched for Astral Projection in his classic text, Autobiography of a Yogi. Astral Projection also crops up in Sufism. Sufis speak of alan almithai, or dimensions created by thought. There are numerous accounts in both the Bible and the Qur'an of Astral Projection experiences. And within the shamanic tradition of the Toltec seeker, this skill was rare and only given to people of power. Rulers, priests and warriors were trained in Astral Projection in order to conquer lands, bend reality, and attain self-mastery. In ancient Egypt, they called the energy body Ka, and priests left special inscriptions on how to astral travel on the rock faces of temple walls. In the Bible, St. Paul describes experiences in non-physical realms which he terms as the third heaven. And he describes the thought-responsive nature of these dimensions, something that's also reported by modern astral projectors. In Tibetan Buddhism, Astral Projection is a central practice for advanced meditators, and it has been utilized as a part of dream yoga and practiced for millennia for the purpose of exploring the nature of reality and as preparation for death and dying. Even the modern traditions, like Theosophy, suggest that humans are multidimensional beings possessing up to seven bodies. I'm referring to an astral body among these as the linga sarira. So Astral Projection has a long and strong specific practice, but sometimes there's still some confusion around it, due to commonalities with other abilities. So let us clear some things up. Astral Projection is not simply a dream or a shamanic journey, remote viewing, mediumship, dissociation, or just vivid imagination. Phenomenologically these things are experienced quite differently. To help explain, it might be useful to think about these experiences as though you were sitting on the sofa, watching a movie. The act of seeing what's on the TV might be thought as remote viewing; the shamanic journey would be watching through 3D glasses. A lucid dream would be to enter the scene itself, whilst mediumship would be to interact with the characters from the sofa. And then there's dissociation which would kind of be to feel floaty and discombobulated whilst trying to watch the TV. Now with astral travel, you can step out of your body, look back, and have a good look at yourself watching the screen or the TV. You can then either float into the TV and experience that reality, or you could go out of your lounge to see what your neighbors are up to. But here's the thing: because many of these experiences happen in an altered state, it's possible to springboard from them into an out-of-body experience, such as going from the lucid dream into Astral Projection. In fact, we learn how to do this in the quest. So how can we benefit from astral travel? I think we can all agree that astral projection sounds out of this world, right? And it is, but it's more than just a cool experience; it has a whole range of benefits that support well-being. It has huge transformative potential, and there are hard stats to back this up. One study reported that 88% of research participants experienced beneficial change after their out-of-body experience happened. In another, more than 300 participants found that 86% experience heightened awareness, in their perception of reality, with 78% noticing long-term sustainable benefits. The biggest potential of OBEs is that it is a spiritual tool to elevate your state of consciousness. In 1943, the psychologist Abraham Maslow published a paper that was set out to be later called "Maslow's Hierarchy of Needs." Maslow saw that the hierarchy of needs as reflecting the journey of human evolution and that self-actualization was an evolutionary step. For some people that missing link in their evolution is provided by an out-of-body experience, a radical path to becoming all that we can be. When we are at a crossroads in life, in need of guidance, and the universe wants to offer us a little nudge, we might find ourselves in a spontaneous out-of-body experience. Barbara needed a nudge towards self-actualization, and found herself in a spontaneous out-of-body experience that changed her life forever. Barbara was a corporate TV executive from the U.S. who was exhausted by the high pressure lifestyle of the media world. And she was drained by the need to always look good and to be the best. One morning at around 5:00 a.m., she awoke from sleep and rose out of her physical body. She found herself flying over what she somehow knew was the city of Giza in Egypt, next to the river Nile. Her energy body landed near the ancient pyramids. Something was roused within her, and she said she felt "This is where I need to be." As if the land itself was calling her. From her point of awareness, she scanned the horizon and saw dusty apartments dotted throughout the old town, but next to them was a KFC chicken shop. "How could they build a KFC so close to a sacred site?" she thought. Maybe it was just her mind glitching, or perhaps her astral vision was somehow distorting. Whatever it was, it surely couldn't be real. So she shifted her awareness and continued to have an extraordinary out-of-body experience. Then when she found herself back in her physical body, something had changed within her. She couldn't forget how the feeling of the land of Egypt had been beckoning her. And soon her day job in corporate TV began to seem increasingly vacuous in the light of her out-of-body experience. Something had changed within her inner world, and she couldn't shake it off. Eventually she heeded the call. She left the corporate world and made a life-changing decision. Barbara quit her job and retrained as a holistic therapist and a tour guide, taking people on trips to sacred places in Egypt. But when she visited Egypt for the first time in her physical body, she managed to locate the exact same place in Giza, the dusty streets near the pyramids that she visited in her OBE. And just as she had seen, there it was: the KFC chicken shop-proof for her at least that in her OBE she really had made a trip to Egypt. Barbara credits, her out-of-body experience with shaking her out of herd mentality, bringing her in alignment with a greater cause and helping her become more of who she really was. It's not just elevating consciousness that OBEs can be good for; the simple act of Astral Projection itself can be such a mind-blowing experience that they're often classed as what is clinically known as an exceptional human experience. An experience of cataclytic gnosis-knowing- that extends the limits of who we are and what we perceive reality to be. A peak experience in which we can touch the numinous. Basically a massive, "What the heck!" moment, and no wonder. In the same way people who have near-death experiences return believing that they're a soul or a spirit, the same can be said for most astral projectors. Everyone of the case studies from my master's research claims that consciousness goes on after death, even those who are atheist or agnostic beforehand. Knowing for yourself that beyond a doubt you are not exclusively limited to your physical body but simply habitually limited to it and that that habit can be broken can be profound. This is one reason why it's considered an exceptional human experience in the sciences of psychology. Research has shown that these types of experiences make us more open-minded, more emotionally mature, and lead to higher levels of happiness and well-being. Tied in with this is usually the visceral experience of awe. In fact, it's one of the highest reported emotions felt during Astral Projection. Once we get over that initial "What the heck!" moment of leaving our physical body, and we relax into the experience, we realize just how awe-inspiring Astral Projection really is. Flying through the sky at the speed of light, meeting dead loved ones on the astral plane, entering into realms and other dimensions. The possibilities are endless. Yes, get ready for one of the most visceral experiences of awe a human being can have. And awe, it turns out, is really good for you. A University of California, Berkeley study found that awe-some experiences increased people's feelings of connectedness and willingness to help others and that experiences of awe can change the course of a life in profound and permanent ways. The University of Toronto researchers found that awe is actually good for our health too as it directly lowers levels of inflammation, the main cause and the exacerbator of many chronic health conditions. There is a phenomenon reported by astronauts known as the overview effect. It occurs when they look back at the earth and they appreciate the vulnerability and the smallness of that pale blue dot spinning in infinite space. The overview effect creates a cognitive shift of perceptual vastness, reframing one's reality and place within it. How we see ourselves and our world changes. The astronauts who report it are forever transformed for the better. Astral projectors report the same thing. I call this the Outerview Effect. When during Astral Projection they glance back at their physical body, just as the astronauts glance back, they realize they are not their physical body, and so they begin to identify less with it and search less with their limitations. Their sense of self expands, leading to a decrease in existential anxiety and a lowering of thanatophobia, fear of death. Dr. Mel Slater's team at Barcelona University showed that even a virtual reality experience mimicking an illusionary OBE can reduce death anxiety. This has a domino effect into other areas of life, such as relationships, our purpose, and our fears. So in a nutshell, what are the benefits of Astral Projection? Astral travel can be harnessed to source answers to problems, insights into illness, guidance with decision-making, healing with grief, and the releasing of fears and limitations. Suffering from burnout? Take that trip to Hawaii. Feeling lonely? Visit that lover across the pond. Heal that trauma? Go to the source. Want adventure? Fly into space. Imagine having your own private jet to people and places that you can visit from the edge of your bed at any time. You are that plane and this quest is your return ticket.

Preparation 2: The 3 Steps to Astral Projection
--------------------
<v ->Hello, and welcome to your quest on astral projection.</v> My name is Jade Shaw, and I'm going to teach you how to fly. You will learn how to self-initiate an out-of-body experience for self-transformation. Astral projection is a secret skill you never knew you had. What if you could access expanded states of consciousness and connect with people and places beyond time and space? Where would you go? Who would you meet? And what would you bring back? In this quest, we learn how the sages of old traditions activate the ability to astral project for insight, guidance, and healing. Bridging science and spirituality, we draw from Western psychology and Eastern traditions to teach you the core principles of modern day astral projection. So here are a few things about what to expect and how this quest works. This is a beginner's experiential program. So whether you haven't had any experiences at all, or if you have had quite a few, it's perfect if you want to start a practice or boost your current one. It teaches the core principles and methods necessary to self-induce an out-of-body experience and then navigate non-physical realms of reality, so that you feel confident, equipped, and ready to fly. By the end of this program, you will have everything you need to have a successful out-of-body experience. This quest will give you a chance to access altered states of awareness and elevate your consciousness, because astral projection is one of the most powerful spiritual tools for transformation. It will help you to overcome fears and anxiety, transcend identification with the physical body, integrate and heal your shadow, heal grief and meet loved ones, achieve soul alignment. This is a 28-day journey toward self-transformation. And this quest is built like a step-by-step manual for astral projection. There will be some theory to lay a firm foundation, but it will mainly be practical exercises. It's a bit like going to a yoga class, except instead of flying with the body, we're flying with the psyche. Some say, the soul. To do this, we focus on three steps. Step one, the first is the mind awake body asleep state. This is a type of altered state, similar to deep trance. When the mind is awake and aware, but the body is completely relaxed, until we cannot feel it anymore. This is like our flight pad from which we'll springboard into astral projection. Step two, this is the vibrational state. This is a transitory precursor experience which occurs just before we leave the body. It can be filled with unusual sights and sensations such as energy and light. Can be very subtle to pretty intense. But either way, it's completely safe. It's sort of like the wind picking us up before we take flight. Step three, the third step is exiting the body. Now, I don't like using the word exit, because it suggests that we're completely leaving which isn't necessarily true, because an aspect of our consciousness, our awareness, stays behind. It's this that keeps the lungs breathing and the heart beating. And it brings you back immediately if your body gets disturbed or distracted, such as when you need to go to the toilet. However, it does very much feel like a separation or an expansion beyond the body when we astral project. So for the sake of ease, I'll refer to exit techniques in step three. We can practice astral projection through deep meditation and powerful trance states. But one of the best ways, especially for beginners, is on the cusp of sleep, because most spontaneous experiences occur at this time. And it's easier to harness because we all sleep, right? Of course, you can apply almost everything that we learn to other deep altered states. So don't think that astral travel can only happen via sleep states, but it is one of the quickest ways to learn the skill. That's why this quest does just that. So we're going to do this by using our nighttime and daytime techniques to prepare the body and mind. Some of which work with cultivating qualities that improve the ability to astral project, such as sustaining attention. Others are directly involved with leaving the body or traveling the astral planes. How well these techniques work depend on our personal psycho-spiritual makeup, what type of person we are, and where we're at in our spiritual journey. For example, if we're a very perceptive person, the visual methods might work better for you, or if we're very felt sense, the kinesthetic ones might give you more success. This is why you will be given a toolbox of techniques related to the three steps, so you can create a bespoke practice personal to you. It will be a case of trial and error as you begin to discover what type of astral projector you are. That's the fun part though, trying all the sweets in the shop and then pick and mix your favorites. Just like in yoga, the teacher can't give you a handstand balance, but they can give you the skill and the wisdom to do it yourself. In the same way, I can't give you an out-of-body experience, but can I give you the tools and techniques to build this skill to self-induce your own experiences? Absolutely. I'll teach you how to transform your world from the edge of your bed. Now let's take a bird's eye view of how that journey will unfold. Week one is preparing our flight pad, learning the foundations, the core principles of astral projection. Emphasis is placed on preparing the body and mind for effective experiences. The two biggest blocks to astral projection are fears and limiting beliefs. So we will address these head on. We will also learn how to create our own projection plans and harness sleep states with mindfulness to increase our chances of going out of the body. This includes mastering step one, the mind awake, body asleep state. In week two, we spread our wings. We learn how to bring on and ride the vibrational state, the transitional doorway between the physical and the non-physical worlds. This involves connecting to our energy body and heightened levels of awareness. This is where you learn how to navigate non-physical realms and see with your astral eyes. We will discover where you can go and what you can experience. In week three, we begin to soar, so get ready to fly. This week covers step three, exit techniques. Different ways in which you can shift beyond the body and enter other planes of reality. You will learn a range of tools to transition to the astral plane. But not only that, we will learn how to transform sleep paralysis and lucid dreaming into a gateway to the multi-verse. And finally, in week four, we begin to fly high. This is where we explore advanced practices, such as shadow integration, soul retrieval, and meeting dead loved ones through astral projection. We will also test our skills by doing an experiment, as well as learning how to safely embody and integrate our experiences back into our everyday life. The Monroe Institute is the world's most renowned research venue for out-of-body experiences. This is where the CIA trained astral projection and remote viewing, and where some of the world's top trainers reside. They have been developing brainwave technology for expanded states of consciousness, such as binaural beats and isochronic tones, for over 40 years. This cutting-edge technology helps to place the brain in the best conducive states for astral travel. Coupled with my guided meditations and exercises, you will be in the best possible place to start your practice. Here are the main things you need to prepare: projection diary and pen. This is a journal or notebook that you dedicate to record your out-of-body experiences. We will also use it for some of the lessons and exercises. Headphones. This quest is full of guided audio recordings that bring you into an altered state of consciousness. An eye mask, earplugs, and cushions and blankets are optional. Also, here are a few of the tips on how to maximize success with your learning journey. I suggest dedicating a specific time on your calendar, 20 to 30 minutes, for watching the videos and doing the daytime exercises, even though most practices will be done at night. Block off that time in your calendar and commit to it for 28 days; make it a non-negotiable. This is your time to invest in yourself. And connect with your tribe; use this conscious community of like-minded individuals to support one another on learning and embodying your new skills towards self-transformation. Set an intention in your projection diary. Why are you here? What do you think might have brought you to this specific course at this specific time? Why do you want to learn astral projection? Is it to align more with your inner self, connect to dead relatives and overcome grief, or transform the fear of death? Maybe take your spiritual practice to the next level. What is it for you? Your actions for today. Before we start our journey, I'd like you to prepare your projection diary, because it will be crucial for our journey together. And another action before we start is to set your intention and write down your motivation for starting this Quest. You can write it, you can paint it, whatever you like; get creative. And then, I suggest to go an extra mile and put it in a visible place so that every time you see it, it can remind you and help you to continue on this journey. We're going to go way beyond to be well within. See you on the other side.

Week 1: Prepare Your Body & Mind

LESSON 1: Start an Astral Projection Diary
--------------------
<v ->Hello, and welcome to your quest on astral projection,</v> aimed at teaching you how to astral travel for the purposes of self-transformation. I've looked back at my physical body, time traveled, shed the fear of death, met ancestors, witnessed the vastness of space, entered other dimensions, healed parts of my soul, and experienced unconditional love. This isn't your average well-being practice. This is a powerful way to evolve your consciousness because it can positively transform the very essence of who you are. I wouldn't be sitting here speaking to you if it didn't. So let me ask you this question: are you willing to let go of who you think you are, so you might become all you can be? The ancient philosopher Lao Tzu said, "The key to growth is the introduction of higher dimensions of consciousness into our awareness." This is what astral projection does. So I hope you're ready because I know what's in store for you, and I'm pretty excited. I've been doing this since I was a child, and still every time I astral travel, it absolutely blows my mind, and I can't wait for you to experience it. Over the next four weeks, I'm going to teach you how to master three steps that will give you the ability to self-induce your own out-of-body experiences and build an astral projection practice. But like any new skill, we have to start from scratch. Walk before we can run which is why it's important to tune in to our intention, check our motivation, and create a projection plan. So grab your projection diary and let's get going. A projection diary is like a dream diary, except we also write about the things that happen throughout the night too, such as what we notice when we drift in and out of sleep, and during any meditations. If you have a dream, sleep paralysis, insomnia, or astral journey, anything that comes up during your practice, it all goes in the diary. This way we can keep track of our progress and notice any significant steps and breakthroughs. You can write in your diary at any time, but I will be specifically asking you to use it for certain activities during the Quest. We're going to do the first one together now. I'd like you to create a projection plan, something you would like to do in your astral projection experiences. So to avoid aimlessly floating around your room when you come out of body, you might want to think about where you want to go and what you want to do. What most people don't realize is that once you self-initiate the out-of-body experience, you have the keys to the universe. You can go anywhere. The possibilities are limitless, and yet beginners often wander around their house because they're not quite sure where to go. So now there's nothing wrong with this. In fact, your first experience is often one that is most memorable anyway. When I was the consultant for the cast of Behind Her Eyes on Netflix, I did a workshop with the actors. The main character Adele, played by Eve Hewson, managed to get her energy head out of her body. She lifted it out and she was so stunned, she dropped back into her body. This is because it felt so real. It is not a dreamy experience at all. So even if you come out and you roam around your room, it probably will be pretty exciting, but let's aim to do something even more adventurous. Creating a projection plan involves deciding on our intention, what we're going to do, and our motivation, why we're going to do it. If I were going to buy a loaf of bread, my intention would be to go buy the bread, but my motivation would be to feed my family. Here's a secret tip, choose a meaningful motivation. Our unconscious mind, our highest self, the universe. God is more likely to get on board and support the experience if you have a good reason to do it. I'm not sure they would probably get on board if you wanted to go spy on your ex or access the lottery numbers. Now I'm not saying don't have fun. On the contrary, a sense of play is very important. So by all means, fly to the moon, time travel, or go visit your friend. But for your main goal, perhaps choose something that you know will make a positive impact in your life or develop your spiritual practice, such as healing grief, overcoming fears, connecting to your purpose, releasing limitations, or developing your psychic awareness, experiencing life after death to lose the fear of death, or accessing infinite possibilities. I'd like you to write the following statement of intent in your diary. Choose the words that resonate most with you, and then fill in the blanks. "I call on my subconscious, highest self, spirit guide, or ancestor to help me go beyond the body to go, see, or experience __________ for the purpose of ____________." Choose what resonates with you the most. Here are a few examples: I call on my subconscious to help me go beyond the body to experience whether this is even really possible for the purpose of exploring states of consciousness. I call on my ancestors to help me go beyond the body to meet my dead father for the purpose of healing grief and gaining closure. I call on my highest self to help me go beyond the body to access other dimensions that show me my ultimate potential. I call on my spirit guide to transcend the body and experience an ultimate feeling of oneness with life and all there is. If you're not quite sure, that's okay. There's no need to force it. It might be that something comes to mind later on today or even in the week, but allow this question to drop into your mind: what do I want to do, and why do I want to do it? Your actions for today. Dedicate five minutes now and fill in the statement of intent in your projection diary. So by the end of today, you will have your projection plan, what you want to do, and why you want to do it. And then, we'll be able to learn some skills to make your plan happen. But that's for tomorrow, I'll see you then.

LESSON 2: The 12 Stages of the Hero's Journey for Astral Projection
--------------------
<v ->Hello, dear travelers.</v> Now that you're charged up with motivation, let's talk about the right attitude and approach to astral projection. In the Harry Potter books, the arch-villain Lord Voldemort strikes down the hero dead with a swipe of his wand. When Harry awakens, he's in a place of bright white light, that looks like King's Cross Station in London. He's having a near-death experience and Dumbledore, his wizard mentor, is there to greet him. After giving him advice, Dumbledore invites Harry to make a decision to stay or to move on or to return to his life. Harry knows he has to go back to finish his mission to defeat Voldemort. But before he leaves, Harry asks Dumbledore, "Is this real, or has this all been happening inside my head?" Dumbledore replies, "Of course it's happening inside your head, Harry, but why on earth should that mean it is not real?" "The Hero's Journey" is a common story structure shared by many cultures worldwide. The mythologist Joseph Campbell studied human myths throughout history and noticed that the same sequence appeared across cultures over and over again. He wrote about this in his book, "The Hero With a Thousand Faces" and he coined it "The Mono Myth" a symbolic universal story that we can all relate to. And it goes something like this: an ordinary person living their habitual and often ordinary life one day experiences something unexpected. This experience sets them off on a quest, a call to adventure. And during this quest, they meet new friends, allies, maybe even an enemy or two, and they face personal challenges. They find a mentor, and they battle for the greater good. And they finally return home, a changed person. Hollywood uses this as the dominant narrative for many of its movies, from Harry Potter to Pocahontas, King Arthur, and to The Lion King. The hero ventures into the unknown, and after a long journey full of dangerous twists and turns, they return triumphantly with the elixir. Almost always the so-called elixir is not what the hero expected, but if anything, it's something even better. In almost all heroic myths, the elixir takes form of some kind of timeless wisdom both for the hero and their community. You are this hero, the main character in your astral projection story. And whether you know it or not, you've already set off on your quest to find the elixir because you're here. This is why we're going to use "The Hero's Journey" as a framework for our progress. It's an empowering way of making sense of where we're at and understanding what might be to come. It's kind of like a mythical roadmap for tracking self-transformation. Now you might be thinking, well, I'm not a hero, I definitely don't feel like one, but that's exactly how the hero starts off. They're a normal person living an ordinary life until they get the call. In the hero's journey, there are 12 stages through which the hero undergoes inner and outer transformation to varying degrees. And although I've applied these stages to astral projection, see if any of them already sound familiar to you. Maybe you've already experienced some of these stages in areas of your life. Stage one, the ordinary world. You're living your normal life, doing all the everyday things as you've been doing them for a long time probably. Stage two, the call to adventure. Something happens to shake you up. There's a threat or a risk that disrupts your world. It can come in many forms: perhaps a loved one has died, your relationship has broken down, or you've lost your job. Or you've been diagnosed with a chronic illness, or maybe you've had something that you don't quite understand yet, like a spiritual awakening experience. Whatever it is, it calls you to take a new direction with life and presents you with something challenging. Maybe even something unwanted; whatever it is, it is the call to adventure, and your quest awaits. In our case here, right here, right now, it's astral projection. Stage three, refusal of the call. So you've heard the call, you know you kind of have to change lanes and move to this new thing, but you might be scared, full of doubts and unsure, unsure if you can handle it. And it feels far more safe to stay where you are in the comfort of what you know, naturally. So you stay where you are for a while longer until you get the call again, and this time you can't really ignore it. Stage four, meeting the mentor. You search for or cross paths with a mentor. Sometimes this mentor isn't an obvious example, but you soon find that in some way they can be a guide or a teacher for you in this moment. Maybe you sought them out or perhaps stumbled upon them by chance; either way, this mentor dispels your fears and gives you the confidence and the tools to set off on this new adventure. Right now, for you in this moment, that mentor is me. Stage five, crossing the first threshold. The threshold is the point where the hero enters new territory. It's not yet the point of no return, but it is very different to the world and life that they're used to. Your first threshold here with me, is taking your first step on your astral projection journey. The second threshold is learning how to do it. This is what we're going to begin this week. Stage six, tests and allies. This is when you're out of your comfort zone. You've gained confidence and knowledge of astral projection and are now putting it into action. But naturally, there might be some barriers along the way. You're still finding your feet; skills need practice, and you might feel like you're being tested. This is when you call on your tribe for support, reach out to the people who you trust and who can support you through this challenge. Know and call upon your allies. Are you going to give up at the first hurdle, or continue on the quest? Stage seven, approach to the cave. Entering the cave is like facing the abyss. This is when people start having their first out-of-body experience, OBE. Here we are being called to be brave and take a leap of faith. This is the point where you commit; bringing all of yourself to this moment, including all the fearful voices that tell you to quit, you keep going. This is our first real taste of entering the unknown, really going for it. Stage eight, the ordeal. Now you, the hero, may face a major challenge. As astral projection is ultimately a practice of self discovery, it could be that you realize something about yourself, have a profound insight, encounter something unexpected, or face a recurring problem. This might make you deeply question things. Sometimes at this stage, we might feel a bit defeated. And in the case of astral projection, you might find that your interest starts to wane, or a voice in your head says, "This isn't for me; it's not worth my time," or "I'm not ready for this." All of these voices are coming from a belief that is I'm not good enough, but there is always a glimmer of hope. In the Hero's Journey, it's the moment of despair before the hero finds the last bit of courage to slay the dragon in the deepest part of the cave. And we all have these dragons. At this time, you need to dig deep, deep into your inner resources, access the energy, the strength, the faith, whatever it is for you that you need to overcome this obstacle. It's never easy, but it is always worth it. Stage nine, the reward. This is your breakthrough moment. You've stuck it out this far, and you've been through some challenges. And suddenly you see this progress, a tipping point. You might feel you've not mastered it yet, but you're doing something that you didn't do before. It could be experiencing deep altered states, your first astral projection experience, or it might be achieving something specific during your astral travel, such as fulfilling your projection plan. For others it could happen before the out-of-body experience takes place. Perhaps you have a profound insight or realization during the practice for astral projection. This is the reward, the breakthrough; it's your breakthrough, it's real and it's important. Stage 10, the road back, you faced your fears and doubts. You've gained your reward, and now comes the journey back home. You prepare for transitioning back to your life before you embark on your quest, and you start to reflect on how you've changed, what you've learned. There'll be some people you say goodbye to, and some who you'll meet again soon, and you might be wondering, why did I learn astral projection? How will it fit into my life? And it's natural if you don't have a vision for where this practice fits yet; all heroes go through these uncertainties as they prepare for the long road back home. Make a note of all these questions and doubts; the answers will come in time, but for now you allow yourself the knowledge that being in the unknown is exactly where you need to be. And ask yourself, what do I need for support, resources, or practices to help me make this long journey on the road back to safety and wellness? Stage 11, the resurrection. At some point on the road back, the hero has one final moment of either challenge or discovery, or both some times. After this, they discover the final piece of the puzzle. And for now they might experience something of a rebirth. In heroic myths, this is often called the Phoenix rising or the resurrection. Sometimes they encounter someone who at one point might have been a bit of a thorn in that side. In your case, it might not be a person, but it could be a familiar inner voice or a doubt, or a fear that comes back to trouble you one last time. This voice might be telling you, you'll never be able to astral project; it's all nonsense. No one will understand you or believe you if you tell them where you've been and what you've done; but having conquered your dragons and having embraced this one last time, you realize you've become a different person. A part of you is remade, reborn, or even alive for the first time. You are not the same person who started this journey when you heard the call; you're ready to be the new you, all that you've learned will be a part of you. And you will thrive in your life because of it. Stage 12, return with the elixir. Remember within the quest, we will all enter these different stages at various times because we're all on our own unique journey. We're all different. Depending on your practice, you might only get through a few of these stages or you might get through them all quite quickly during our time together; there's no right or wrong pace. And there isn't a prize for who gets to stage 12 first; we can't force the hero's journey; it unfolds in its own time when we go through the training and do our practices. Also, your astral projection quest will continue after you finish this course, so there's no pressure to get to the end. LESSON 3: Overcome the 3 Common Fears of an Out of Body Experience
--------------------
<v ->Hello, and welcome back heroes.</v> Joseph Campbell, the author of "The Hero with a Thousand Faces" famously said, "The cave you fear to enter holds the treasure you seek." Today, we're going to explore something many of us instinctively shy away from, the F word. So let's do the best thing for fear; let's embrace it by naming it and facing it. It's a perfectly natural response to feel fear about new things that we haven't tried before. We're human after all. And in this session, we'll look at the top three fears related to OBEs, out-of-body experiences, why we feel this fear, and how maybe we can transform it. Before we go on, what is the thing or things you fear the most? Not just your big fears, but small day-to-day worries too. You see, how we react to fear in life is probably how we'll respond to astral projection in some way. Are you aware of your fears and where they come from? When you experience fear, where does it sit in your body and how do you respond? Do you feel fear about having an out-of-body experience, or perhaps you don't feel any at all, or maybe there's a subtle fear occurring for you? The irony is, there have been many anecdotes from astral projectors who have reported a reduction in fear and anxiety, especially death anxiety, after experiencing the astral plane, myself included. Fear is completely normal when it comes to this type of work. So you're not alone. And although it can be one of the biggest stumbling blocks to astral projection, it's something that we can actually work to our advantage. Tibetan Buddhist nun, Pema Chodron, author of "The Places That Scare You," says, "Fear is a natural reaction to moving closer to the truth." So maybe in some instances it's nudging us towards something that we need to look at within ourselves. There are a range of tools I'm going to share with you today to help overcome any fear you might have about experiencing astral projection. More about that in a moment though. First of all, what is fear? Fear is a natural and primitive emotion. It alerts us to the presence of danger or the threat of harm, whether that danger is physical or psychological. Sometimes fear stems from real threats, but it can also originate from imagined dangers, like when we see things in the dark. Of course, fear can also be a symptom of some mental health conditions too. Did you know, we're only born with two fears: falling and of loud noises. Sometimes we can have the sensation of falling when falling asleep, which can cause an involuntary body reaction, such as hypnic jerks. Maybe you've had this experience, this kind of like jolting sensation as you're drifting off and falling asleep. But today we're going to specifically explore the fear connected to having an out-of-body experience, either beforehand in the waking state or in those moments as it's happening. Firstly, it's important to remember that fear is there to help us. Though of course, sometimes our fear can be misguided like an over-protective parent. Fear is unhealthy when it makes you more cautious than you really need to be to stay safe and when it prevents you from doing the things you would otherwise enjoy. But it is a natural emotion and a survival mechanism. When we confront a perceived threat, our bodies respond in specific ways. So it's a helpful emotional response. Physical reactions to fear include sweating, increased heart rate, high adrenaline levels that make us extremely alert. If you have a phobia such as spiders, like me, you might have experienced this before. But sometimes this can happen when we're about to have an out-of-body experience, 'cause we've never had one before. This physical reaction is also known as the fight or flight response, which your body prepares itself to either enter combat or run away. This biochemical reaction is likely an evolutionary development. It's an automatic response that is crucial to our survival. So it's perfectly normal human response to have in a wide range of circumstances. Some people are adrenaline seekers, thriving on extreme sports and other fear-inducing thrill situations. Others have a negative reaction to the feeling of fear and avoid fear-inducing situations at all costs. I'd like to share a story with you now called The Hunter and the Thorn, which exemplifies a lesson linked to this avoidance of fear that I'd like us to learn. The Hunter and the Thorn. A man was out hunting in the woods when he shot a deer. But in the process, he caught his arm on a thorn bush. He cried out as the thorn stuck deep in his arm, but he was too scared of the pain that it might cause if he tried to pull it out. So he decided to not move his arm at all and instead strapped it to his side. But, he couldn't manage to drag the deer with one arm, so he had to leave his catch behind. On his way home, he came to a thick part of the woods where he accidentally brushed his arm on a nearby tree. In anger, he decided to avoid this area and find a different way back. He arrived home late without food, and his family went without supper that night. In the morning, he awoke to find that his arm had healed with the thorn inside it. But it had hit a nerve causing pain in other areas of his body. Without being able to use his arm, he couldn't physically work, and so he had to look for another job which he was given less pay. This troubled the hunter who couldn't use his full potential and he worried about what he was going to do. How different might his life have been if he had just pulled out the thorn? This is a simple example of how fear and the avoidance of pain and suffering can shape our life in unseen ways. We could be the hunter, and the thorn may be the fear lodged in our mind restricting access to our greater potential and our ability to astral project. But we are in a much better position than the hunter because we can choose to turn towards the thorn and see it. And sometimes this is enough to even release it. But for those deeper thorns, which we all have to some degree, we can build the courage to pull them out. So if you're thinking, "Well, I don't have any thorns," that might be the case, but also, we might have some invisible thorns that were lodged in so long ago we've forgotten that they're there. So if we discover any in today's session or over the next few weeks, let's get those tweezers ready and be compassionately curious about what rosebush the thorn came from. So how might these thorns, these fears, interrupt astral projection? In short, our fear response in our body keeps us in our body. So let's look at three common fears of having an out-of-body experience. The first, will I come back to my physical body? This is an underlying fear of, will I die? Number two, will I return altered in some way? The underlying fear here is, will I lose my mind? Number three, can I go where I want? Will I have full control? What do you notice about all of these things? They're all fears related to the unknown. For those who've had an OBE before, you might not be asking these questions or feeling these fears because for you, it's not an unknown. Do you relate to any of these top-three fears, or perhaps you have a different concern? Take a minute or two now to write down in your diary any fear you might have; name it. That's the first step to removing the thorn. Philosopher Ralph Waldo Emerson said, "Knowledge is the antidote to fear." So I'm going to give you that gift right now. Here are the short answers to those big fears. Will I come back to my physical body? Yes; yes, you will. Your consciousness is automatically drawn to its physical body. In fact, it's harder to stay out of body once we're in astral projection. OBE teacher and author, Graham Nicholls, reckons it's around 20 minutes when we begin to habitually shift back into the body. However, because we experience time differently during astral projection, it could feel like much longer or much shorter, but rest assured, you will come back to your body. Look at it this way. At some point, you're going to want to go to the toilet. So that will definitely bring you back. Could I lose my mind? Will I return altered in some way? No, you won't lose your mind, but it's highly likely you will return changed for the better with new insights and wisdom. Like in the return of the hero's journey, sometimes the return can be challenging because we've learned something new about ourselves or the world. So we do need to integrate any new insights into our life and ground back into this reality here and now. Towards end of the Quest, I'll be sharing some ways in which we can do this together. Will I have control? This is a tricky one. The answer is both yes and no. But no isn't a bad thing. In the same way we don't have control over everything in our lives, when we're in the astral plane, we don't have control over everything there, but we do have control over our own actions, and we can choose to leave at any time we wish. You can steer the ship on the astral plane in the same way your mind sails through waking life. And I'll be giving you some tips later for greater control. Now, what if you're overwhelmed with fear just before or during astral projection? In that moment, when you feel the fear take over, what do you do? We take a Metta-Moment. Metta is a loving kindness meditation, and it can help us to shift quickly from the lane of fear to the lane of love. Now we probably won't have time to do a whole Metta meditation right now, but we can take a Metta-Moment. Let's give it a go together now. Close your eyes and drop your awareness into your heart center. Bringing attention to the chest space and tuning into the energy of the heart. You might like to do this by feeling your heartbeat or acknowledging your capacity for love, a capacity which we all have. Sometimes it might be tricky to do this quickly, especially if we're filled with fear. So what can help is thinking of people, pets, or places that you're grateful for. Bring them to mind now. Feel the feelings you have for them, and let these feelings wash over you. And if you'd like to, perhaps send them a smile from your heart. Okay, open the eyes. It's as simple as that. You can take a Meta-Moment whenever you need. With astral projection, one of these times might be when you're about to enter the unknown. Rumi said, "What is fear? The non-acceptance of uncertainty, if we accept uncertainty, it becomes adventure." Gosh, I remember the first time that I experienced the vibrational state, I was so scared. I had this energy flowing through the body. I was hearing these strange sounds. I didn't know what to do. But now when I feel it, I know what's happening. So I'm like, okay, here we go. Roll up my sleeves; let's do this. But what we don't know, we can't control, right? And more often than not, what we do know, we can't control either. LESSON 4: Break Limiting Beliefs About Astral Projection
--------------------
- Hello, and welcome back. Yesterday, we addressed our fears, and today, we're setting our unhelpful beliefs free. An unhelpful belief is a limiting belief which is exactly how it sounds. A limiting belief is a thought, a state of mind, an opinion that we believe to be true and limits us in some way. They usually have some kind of negative impact on our lives by preventing us from moving forward or growing on a personal, professional, or spiritual level. You know the score; we've been doing this since we were kids, we make up a story about the why, or the what, or what we've been told by a caregiver or a teacher. And then we take it as fact, until we start to live our life as though this story were true. Often it's because we believe it's keeping us safe, but the truth is these stories are preventing us from flourishing. More often than not, limiting beliefs keep you from reaching your most significant potential. They can get in the way of what you think is possible for yourself. Are you ready to let go of and clear the limiting beliefs that could be keeping you from achieving so much more? Let's jump right in. So, in terms of astral projection, how might these limiting beliefs be showing up? On the surface, they might sound like this. The avoider often makes excuses. "I just don't have enough time to practice." "Oh, it's going to disturb my sleep." "I've heard it's dangerous." They avoid through distraction, excuses, and making themselves busy. The victim usually plays small. "I'm never any good at these things." "It won't happen for me, so why bother trying?" "It will take me ages to learn." They keep themselves small. The catastrophizer believes the worst. "What if I don't come back to my physical body?" Or, "Surely I'm going to go mad." They catastrophize future events. The mental filterer focuses on the negative. "I came out of my body and I went on a journey into the universe, but I didn't do my projection plan, I didn't do all my things, what a waste of time." They fail to recognize the little wins, and so they don't celebrate their achievements. The demander puts pressure on themselves such as, "I've been practicing for ages, I ought to have had an OBE by now." "I should be able to meditate." "I must be able to learn more techniques." They use demanding language to punish themselves into success. Now, I don't know about you, but I've definitely experienced all of those things in the past. But there's usually a dominant one, isn't there, or two, that we fall into the most. For me, it's the mental filterer. And I know it's related to having quite a strong inner critic. I'm a recovering perfectionist, so I struggle with not getting great results straight away, but that's me. Which one sounds more like you? If you listened to those types and you sat there thinking, "Oh, oh, that one's me." Don't worry, we all start out here. These are very common limiting beliefs, especially amongst beginners. And the great thing we can do is be able to release some of these beliefs. If you identified with the avoider, practice self-discipline, set an achievable task that's realistic for you. Maybe writing one sentence in your projection diary every day. Also not comparing yourself to others in the tribe, it will only set you in a position to justify why you should avoid practice. Besides, remember we're all diverse heroes on different journeys. You can't compare Batman to Moana, can you? If you resonated with the victim, be aware of your words, for words are spells that shape our reality. So, cast a good one. Instead of saying, "This is too hard for me," maybe say, "Wow, what an exciting challenge." Reframe how you see yourself; it will make the situation much easier. Don't forget all heroes go through tough patches too, so it might just be one for you. If you are a catastrophizer, rather than focusing on what could go wrong, focus on what might go right. What if I do come out of my physical body and fly through the clouds? Can you be open to possibilities that seem out of your reach? If you focus on the negatives like the mental filterer, practice gratitude, celebrate the positives. You might find it hard to do at first, but try to notice the things that go right. Take a moment to acknowledge it because even the smallest progress is a movement towards your goal. It's the tortoise that wins the race, remember, not the hare. So, if you demand a lot from yourself, just take it easy. The demander. If you demand a lot from yourself, take the foot off the pedal and relieve the pressure, practice patience, and go lightly with yourself. Rather than using should have, would have, couldas, adopt a gentle language, lean into softness. Listening to and letting go of our limiting beliefs is moving closer to our liberation. Now, we know what type of limiting beliefs that we might have, let's take a few minutes to assess them. In a moment, I'd like you to pause this video while you take note of your limiting beliefs in relation to astral projection. LESSON 5: The First Step: Mind Awake Body Asleep
--------------------
<v ->Hello, astral travelers.</v> So far, we've looked at our expectations, our fears, our limiting beliefs, and our mindset in preparation for astral projection. If we apply what we've learnt so far and throughout the rest of the Quest, it will enable us to have quicker, longer, and deeper experiences. So now let's remember the three steps to astral projection. Step one is the mind awake body asleep state. This is the altered state of awareness we first need to get into to astral travel. Step two is the vibrational state. This is the transitory precursor experience that often happens just before we leave the body. And step three is the most exciting part: this is the sense of separation, expansion, the act of moving beyond the body. Now don't worry about step two or three right now; we need to master step one. This is because if we don't harness this state, it's very hard to astral project, unless of course it happens spontaneously. The mind awake body asleep state is a type of altered state similar to trance; it's when the mind is awake and aware, but the body's completely relaxed, ideally to the point where we can't feel it anymore, what we call total body dissolution. Think of something in the past where you have felt deeply relaxed, almost like you're melting into the space around you. So just having a massage, a warm bath, or being snug in blankets. We want our mind not to feel the boundary of our body anymore so we can't sense where we are in space. It's a bit like when we doze off in the car or the train, your mind is trying to remain alert so that we can get off at the right stop, but your body is nodding off, wanting to go to sleep. We want to get to that point, except with total focus, not letting our mind drift off but staying concentrated. So it's much deeper than a daydream or being very relaxed. I've got some good news for you. You already do it, you just don't know it. It's called the hypnagogic and hypnopompic state. We pass through this state twice a day without even knowing. It's when we enter the hypnagogic, when we're falling asleep and the hypnopompic, when we're waking up from sleep. Of course, we can also use meditation and deep relaxation to self-induce these experiences. But for beginners, harnessing that cusp of sleep is often easier because we do it anyway. Now, if you're sitting there thinking, "Well, I have terrible insomnia, this won't work for me." Actually, it could work for you more than others and this is because the more nightly wake-ups we have, the more chances we have to build the habit of astral projection. Let me explain. It's said that the light bulb inventor Edison used to sit holding ball bearings in his hand, and then he would enter the hypnagogic state, and his body would fall asleep. So he would drop the ball bearings which would jerk him awake, and he could write down any insights from this state for his creative ideas. This is because when we enter the hypnagogic, we often go into the alpha and theta brainwaves, the same sort of ones we enter into when we're having a relaxing massage, using our imagination, or being creative. When this happens, you might begin to get hypnagogic hallucinations. Let me ask you this. Have you ever experienced any of these things on the onset of your sleep? Colors, spirals, geometric patterns, faces, even glimpses of dream imagery. You might even have auditory hallucinations, hear voices, even your name being called. For me, that's how I know I'm on the hypnagogic highway. At one end of the hypnagogic highway, we're awake, and at the other end, we are asleep. Now, as we drift off, we begin to cruise down the highway. Now, we might lose consciousness, black out, and fall asleep and if that happens, maybe that's what our body and mind needs at that time. So whilst it's not great for astral projection, it's okay if that happens. But we might also cruise down the highway, remain aware as we fall asleep, and then enter into a dream or a lucid dream which is a dream in which we know we are dreaming. This is really cool when it happens, because as you're falling through the hypnagogic, you begin to see the dream form all around you: floor, table, window, chair, then pop, you're suddenly in the dream. It's absolutely nuts, and it's so much fun; you can do all sorts of things. But if we cruise along the hypnagogic highway and before we fall asleep, we enter what I call the Goldilocks conditions, not too awake, not too asleep, what I call the sweet spot. If we hit this and at that time we do an exit technique, we can go into astral projection where we leave the body. It's a bit like yoga nidra, the yoga of sleep. I teach this mindfulness approach to astral projection, not only as part of preparation, but also for navigating the experience itself. Mindfulness is being aware of what is happening as it's happening with no judgment or preference. It's like a purposeful way of paying attention to the present moment. This is important for the success of the methods that we will use to self-induce astral travel. This helps us to track our progress better and not get distracted. The body drops off to sleep, but our mind stays conscious. So like Edison, we're going to try and drift on the edge of sleep. LESSON 6: Master the Mind Awake Body Asleep State
--------------------
<v ->Welcome back.</v> How are you doing? How was the mindfulness technique that you tried last night? This practice is foundation to the art of astral projection. And whilst we touch on it, pretty lightly so far, it will become central to cultivating the mind awake body asleep state. Although we've just learnt about this state, today is all about mastering it. Now that's not going to happen overnight; it could take days or weeks, depending on our psychological makeup and how much we choose to practice. This is why we're going to look at some common problems so that if they happen, you know how to handle them. It's like learning to ride a bike. Naturally, the first few times we're probably going to fall off, and that's okay. We need to find the best bike for our body, and then get used to the pedals, the balance, and the speed. This is like finding the right OBE tools for our personality, and then practice, practice, practice. Remember the Hero's Journey: this is the montage scene, the part when Luke Skywalker is practicing in the woods with Yoda, the part where Rocky is getting up at sunrise to train, and the part where Erin Brockovich is learning about law to win her case. Remember, you've just started learning these skills. Here are three common problems that you might have and solutions so that you can solve them. Number one, ego resistance. You might find that you get all ready to practice, and then you need the toilet. You have to scratch an itch. You remember that the washing needs doing, or even the sound of your own breath suddenly begins to get annoying. Sometimes these things do just happen, like the itch, but other times it can be our ego. When our ego is about to enter into the unknown or do something new, it will often attempt to distract us, because subconsciously it's worried about what might happen, and it wants to get back to comfort, back to familiarity. Now, when I say ego, I'm referring to the psychoanalysis perspective. What Freud said, simply put, the ego is that part of our mind that tries to match our hidden desires and wishes with the demands of the real world; it's made up of our experiences, opinions, and our preferences. It creates a sense of personal identity, and this protects us; it helps us to survive in the world. So on one hand, it's a good thing, but sometimes it can get us into trouble. But the ego isn't bad; he just wants to keep us safe, a bit like an over-protective parent. It's well-meaning and keeps us away from danger but maybe doesn't allow us to grow, to take on risks. So if you notice many distractions, or you find yourself becoming quite irritable, you might want to ask yourself, is this my ego? If you intuit that it is, I invite you to have a conversation with it. I treat it like a friendly sidekick, sort of like Watson to Sherlock Holmes, Louise to Thelma, or Woody to Buzz Lightyear. You know they've got your back, but they might stop you from doing something they perceive puts you in peril. But the thing is they need your encouragement and curiosity to take them out of their comfort zone, to rise to the challenge. They, the ego, will probably be reluctant at first, but deep down they know that ultimately it will do them good. When we get our egoic sidekick onboard, we become a powerhouse of unstoppable energy. So give it a go. When you're realizing you're distracting yourself, or you're avoiding your practice or becoming quite irritable, take a moment to have an internal chat with your ego, your sidekick, and see what it says. Number two, clicking out. Occasionally you might find that you have a lapse in consciousness during an exercise. It's a bit like momentarily falling asleep, but it feels lighter. For example, you're following a guided meditation, and you lose consciousness, but then suddenly you find yourself back, but at a different point in the meditation, and you're like, how did I get here? Robert Monroe called this clicking out. We lose concentration and we drift off somewhere. It's like zoning out and having a daydream, a daydream that we can't recall. To combat this we need to improve our concentration skills, so that we don't easily get pulled away from what we're doing. The ability to gently hold our attention will not only allow us to enter deeply into the mind awake body asleep state, but it will also help increase our recall, enable more control both in astral projection and our everyday life, because it improves our focus. To do this we're going to learn dharana. This is a one pointed focus meditation from the Yoga Sutras of Patanjali, and it means concentration of the mind in Sanskrit. Simply put, it's the basic action of holding our attention, binding the mind to one thing that could either be externally, so we could look at an object, or internally, such as an idea, feeling, or even hypnogogic imagery. When I was six, my dad taught me how to do this, but to be honest, I didn't really know what I was doing. My bedroom was forest-themed, and at the end of my bed, I had a poster of a tropical jungle. I would glare intensively at a tree, trying not to think of anything at all, giving myself eye strain, and then a thought would come, and I'd shift onto the next tree and I'd start again. I was sort of doing it right, but there was far too much strenuous staring. So here's how to do it right. You can practice dharana anywhere, but wherever you choose to do it, find a comfortable, seated or standing position, one that doesn't take too much effort to stay in. You can choose to close your eyes and focus on something within you, perhaps your astral projection intention, or an affirmation, or you can anchor your mind to a picture or an object in front of you. Imagine giving your mind the freedom to roam around, but in a very restricted area, you can start with a wider area to begin with, such as a large picture frame. And as you progress, you can bring the area smaller, so your concentration becomes smaller and smaller, such as focusing on a candle flame. When thoughts start coming in or muscles start twitching, the mind tends to follow these sensations, and our concentration can be lost. If this happens, it's okay; just bring your mind back again. This is just the monkey mind jumping around which it naturally does. The mind is like a muscle that we can train. We keep getting back on the bike every time we fall off. So at one point in the future, we can ride our bike without stabilizers. I'd like you to do this for a few minutes at some point today. So select your place and what you're going to focus on and when you're going to do it. Three, the emotional mind. When we experience something new, we might become really excited, super scared, or maybe somewhere in between. In fact, the two most commonly reported feelings on out-of-body experiences is awe, awe of where we go and what we see during the experience, and fear, usually of the unknown. This emotional overwhelm can happen just before an out-of-body experience. Often on the cusp of transition, at the vibrational state, especially if we haven't had an experience before and we don't know what to expect. It can end up snapping us out of whatever altered state we're in and bring us back into the body. So remaining calm and collected is key to success. One time I had a really unexpected and fast exit from the body. It's just that often, on the onset of exiting and shortly after separation, that intense feelings can bring us back to the body. So here's an affirmation that you can say in a moment of emotional overwhelm: I release control. I surrender to the flow. I release control. I surrender to the flow. It's vital that you try to connect with a real felt sense of letting go and surrender. Actually do it. If you're saying I release control, I surrender to the flow, you're still full of fear, and it's not going to happen. Empty words won't work, because it's about the energy that they evoke from the meaning that we give them and the feelings that we have upon saying them that will transform the space. Basically, we want to feel what we're saying rather than just saying it. So if at any point you feel overwhelmed with emotion, whether it's in the mind awake body asleep state, or you're about to leave the body, try the affirmation. Four, falling asleep and waking up. You will also still be getting all of the meditative benefits, but let's try avoid falling asleep. This is called Progressive Muscular Relaxation. Dr. Edmund Jacobson invented this technique way back in the 1920s as a way to help his patients deal with anxiety. He was a man ahead of his time. He knew that relaxing the muscles could relax the mind as well. The exercise involves working through each muscle group, first tensing and then releasing them. It usually starts with the feet and works the way up through the body slowly. By tensing and releasing specific limbs, we're more aware of the tension that we hold that we had no idea that was there. As we let this go in our mind, we let that part of our body go too. We allow it to dissolve away. Often, people that have been stressed out for a long time don't actually know that they're tense. But if you ask them to intentionally create tension and then release it, newfound awareness of what relaxation can feel like can then be experienced and absorbed. This is great for the mind awake body asleep state. It can be done at any time, but if we practice it whilst we're drifting towards the hypnagogic, it can lead to a deep state quickly. When we practice this, really feel the tension draining away from those muscles as though they're just melting away. Hello, and welcome to the progressive muscular relaxation exercise. What we're going to do is tense each part of our body, from our feet to our head, one by one for a few seconds. Now, tense as much as you can. Remember, we want to tire out the body so that it falls asleep. You can either do this standing up, or you can do it lying in bed. Week 2: Learn to Fly

====================

LESSON 8: Tune Into the Energy Body for Astral Projection
--------------------
<v ->Welcome back.</v> Today, we are talking about energy. I'd like to start with this astonishing quote by astrophysicist Neil deGrasse Tyson. He says, "The atoms of our bodies are traceable to stars that manufactured them in their cores, and exploded these enriched ingredients across our galaxy billions of years ago. For this reason, we are biologically connected to every other living thing in the world. We are chemically connected to all molecules on earth, and we are atomically connected to all atoms in the universe. We are not figuratively, but literally, stardust." Well, less than 1% of us is stardust; actually the rest is empty space. Everything is made of energy. The sun, the moon, your mum, everything. Many traditions around the world have versions of energy systems that run through the body, from chi in traditional Chinese medicine to prana in the Indian schools of yoga. They believe that we have an energy body meshed with the physical one within which energy flows freely. For example, you might have heard of the chakra system which is an example of this. Through our life experiences, this vital energy can become clogged and blockages can occur which treatments and practices such as acupuncture, reiki, and yoga can help with. Most of the time we're not really in tune with the energy body; we live in our minds, don't we? Thinking about the past, or the future, what we're going to make for dinner, or what we should have said or not said in the argument that we had, we lose sense of our body, our sematic awareness. So, although we talk about going out of body, we're very rarely connected to it anyway in our everyday life. Paradoxically, in order to have a successful out-of-body experience we need to build a relationship in body. Otherwise, we cannot tune into our energy system or safely ground back when we return from astral travel. It is this bioenergy part of us from which the energy body during an OBE is created. Tibetan Buddhist scholar and dream yoga expert, Alan Wallace, calls it an ethereal body which he says is projected out into ordinary reality. He says, "What you send out is not some ghostly emanation, not the intuitive power of clairvoyance; you are actually sending something out that is physical and imbued with your awareness and localized." From this point of view, we project our conscious awareness away from the body in a non-physical but tangible form. The Dalai Lama said, "Consciousness can be trained to leave the physical body." And this is what we're training to do. This energy body is sometimes called the subtle or second body, or referred to as the projectable double. There are also different types of OBEs, so different ways in which we experience this double body. And sometimes it's not like a body at all; we can actually just be a floating point of perception with no shape or form. Some people experience the energy body in the felt sense, like a vibration, a floating sensation, tingling feeling. Others might experience it more visually, see a body of light or a cloud of color like an aura. And others might intuitively know that it's there; it's very subtle. But generally, the deeper the trance state, the stronger the energy body will be. Different traditions talk about different types of bodies, such as emotional bodies, mental bodies. But to be honest, all we rarely need to know at this stage is about three of them, the core ones which you're most likely to experience. These are the dream body, the etheric body, and the astral body. The dream body is what we enter into when we fall asleep and we're dreaming. It's usually experienced the same way as the physical body; it looks and feels fleshy and physical most of the time. Of course because it's a dream, weird stuff might happen. The body can change, we can become a giant or tiny, we might have a robot arm, we might grow a pair of wings or even become a zombie. But generally, the dream body looks and feels the same as the physical one. Due to this, dream sex is experienced the same way as in the physical too. Important to flag this up because it's not the same as in the astral, which we'll come to in a bit. The dream body is also the same when we're in a lucid dream which is a dream in which we know we're dreaming. Due to realizing, "Oh, I'm in a dream," we might have more control and the ability to influence things such as shiftshaping our body, but it's still very much experienced in the same way as the physical one, here and now. For example, one time I got lucid, and I changed my body to a man's to see what it would feel like. It was good, but I definitely prefer being a woman. Another time when I used to dance, I practiced no-handed cartwheels in the lucid dream state. And I scraped my hand along the floor; it stung and it bled as it would have done in the real world. Our dream body reflects the physical one and everything that comes with it. The etheric body is very much tied to the real world, what we call physical matter reality or the human realm. It's like the energetic duplicate of this body. And although it's non-physical, it generally has a feeling of mass, a kind of density to it. I often describe it like a heavy shadow or a fat cloud, and it can float and it can fly, so it's malleable and has a tangibility to it. So, it's different to the dream body in that it doesn't appear physically real. There's no flesh to touch, no hands to clap. In fact, they'd probably go through each other, but you might feel a pressure, so there's still a sort of sense, a weight to it. Some teachers say the etheric body is like a low-powered projection. It can kind of collapse on the floor after exiting the body, and sometimes it feels like you're wading through mud when you move forwards. I've experienced both of those things; it's like I'm trudging to the window and other times I can fly, but sometimes I'm slow and clumsy, and I fly like a drunk Superman. However, there are ways to power up the etheric body.
