LESSON 9: Enter & Ride the Vibrational State for Triggering OBEs
--------------------
<v ->Fellow travelers, grab your sails</v> and fasten your parachutes because today we're going to ride the winds of the Vibrational State. I'm going to share with you everything you need to know about this Vibrational State. When it happens, how it happens, and how you can work with it to sail into the astral plane. But what is the Vibrational State? Before you fully enter an out-of-body experience, more often than not, you'll transition through the Vibrational State first. This is an energetic gateway that you pass through in order to become out of body. It's the stage of phasing from the physical into the non-physical. But how can we recognize it? For some, it can be like a gentle or subtle hum or the sensation a bit like if a bee was buzzing inside of us. But for others, it can be more intense. It can feel like you're in a vacuum or like a rocket or you might experience this flurry of energy or almost like lightning electricity flowing through your body. You might even hear voices or sounds like radio frequencies. There might be flashes of color, bright white lights. And you might have one dominant sensation such as the vibrations, several symptoms all at once, like light and energy. When I was a child, it felt like someone had grabbed the edge of my bed and was shoving it back and forth, quite erratically, and I ran down the stairs to say to my mom if she'd been shaking my bed. And so it can feel that intense. But now, it feels like a subtle hum, tiny waves rippling through my body. But if you were to see me in the Vibrational State, I wouldn't be moving at all. It would look like I was just fast asleep. These are internal sensations that feel extremely real. The experience can be vastly or subtly different from one person to the next. But generally, the overarching signature of the Vibrational State is a felt sense of physical feeling, sometimes with a visual aspect too, and often involves this sense of vibration. Think of it like the white noise of a radio before tuning into a new channel, except you are the radio and the new channel is your new reality. To understand this, it might be worth knowing what it is and what it isn't. There are five things that you might experience that could be confused with the Vibrational State. One, exploding head syndrome. Exploding head syndrome is a rare parasomnia in which the affected person is startled from sleep with the sensation of a loud noise, like a bang. But don't worry. The head doesn't actually explode. It has been described as a painless, loud bang, a clash of cymbals, or kind of like a bomb exploding. I've had this a couple of times and it's pretty alarming. Both times, it was a one instant sensation, like someone had whacked me over the head with a wooden plank or kind of like a gunshot was firing. You wake up going, "Oh my God, what was that?" It's quite shocking, but it's within a moment. Researchers don't know why exploding head syndrome happens. And sometimes it can be confused with headache syndromes, but it's normally painless and it has no lingering pain. Two, an epileptic fit. This is a seizure that can happen whilst awake or asleep, suffered by someone with epilepsy. It can look like an uncontrollable shaking and jerking. The person might collapse and lose awareness and not remember what's happened. Despite feeling uncannily real, the Vibrational State is an internal sensation. We don't actually move through it physically although it could feel like a seizure of sorts. Three, restless legs. You have the urge to move your arms and legs. They feel twitchy, tingling, like little bugs are creeping under the skin. You might be experiencing restless legs if you feel this. This is also known as Willis-Ekbom Disease. It's a disorder that causes an uncontrollable urge to move your arms and legs, and it typically happens in the evening or nighttime hours when you're sitting or lying down. If you suffer with this, I empathize, because I do too. If you're a highly sensitive person, or you're low on iron, or you have kidney issues, or maybe you're pregnant, you might experience restless leg syndrome. Depending on the cause, moving can ease this unpleasant feeling temporarily. Sometimes, iron or magnesium supplements can help with this, too. Apparently, masturbation can alleviate the symptoms due to the dopamine release. So, you know, if you run out solutions. Four, your heartbeat and blood flowing around the body. The echo-free chamber at Orfield Labs in Minnesota is nicknamed "the quietest place on earth." It absorbs 99.99% of sound, meaning you can hear your heartbeat, your lungs breathe, and your stomach digest. It's really freaky. However, similar things can happen when we're in a deep meditation state. You might hear your own heartbeat or feel your digestion. You can tune into the intricate movement of blood flowing around your body. Because when we're attempting to be totally relaxed, but alert at the same time, noticing these things can happen in the Mind Awake Body Asleep State. And it can sometimes be mistaken for the Vibrational State. This is why practice is key so we know the difference. Five, the hypnagogic and hypnopompic states. You already know what the hypnagogic state is, that drowsy in-between stage where auditory sounds such as voices, imagery, and conceptual dream-like displays occur as you drift off to sleep. These hallucinations are usually made up of memories in the day, mental preoccupations, and the displays of the mind's content. The Vibrational State doesn't usually contain dream-like images. It's more of a psychical sense of subtle movement, energy, and frequency. You might notice light and vibration or varying sounds, and it can differ from time to time. For me, it sounded like the wooden bow of an old ship creaking; but another time, there was a high pitch radio frequency; and another time, it felt like a balloon bursting. So be open to any sensations. But will you always pass through the Vibrational State? Beginners usually experience the Vibrational State more intensely than advanced practitioners. But, some don't seem to enter it all. And actually, once you've had quite a few OBEs, out-of-body experiences, the Vibrational State may feel far less noticeable. Some researchers explain the decreasing sensations over time as kind of an unsticking. It's as though the glue has softened after a few OBEs, and it becomes easier and more subtler to detach or unstick your energy body from the physical one the more we practice it. So when does the Vibrational State occur? It usually happens spontaneously when you are deep in that sweet spot of the Mind Awake Body Asleep State. It can occur though during meditation or deep relaxation and on the cusp of sleep. Though, some astral projectors have reported experience it during the waking state, ordinary reality, but this is very rare. How do we bring on the Vibrational State? When transitioning from Mind Awake Body Asleep into the Vibrational State, it's quite an artful move. It's easy to bypass it completely and head straight into sleep. However, there is a small window of opportunity, and the idea is to sail through that window because when it's open, it can often come on spontaneously. However, we can bring it on through various breathing, visualization, and active imagination techniques, like the ones that you'll follow in the guided audio today. If you start to experience it, the best thing to do is what surfers do which is relax and then ride the wave as it reaches you. So you want to escalate the overall vibrational feeling, the buildup of energy. It's like your body is kind of powering up, and we want to encourage that in some way, encourage these sensations to get more and more. Sometimes, we may only feel them in one part of our body, or they might come and go erratically. So escalate that feeling. If this happens, gently move the vibrations to other areas of your body using your mind and your intent. Now you might be thinking, "How do I move something with my mind?" Through intention and direction. It sort of happens of its own accord, to be honest, and it can be pretty hit and miss, because this state is so fleeting. But as long as you don't have strong emotions or thoughts which can kind of wipe the state away, it should work. How do we approach the Vibrational State when it's happening? Mindfulness teacher and author Clive Holmes has a wonderful butterfly analogy. I always like to use this as a way to explain the best mindset to adopt during the Vibrational State. It's similar to the art of catching a butterfly. A butterfly is very likely to fly off if we try to grab it. If you keep your hands still, the butterfly might temporarily land on your hand, but then fly off again. But if you move your hand steadily and slowly towards the butterfly, you can tentatively catch it. It's almost as though you're not really looking at it at all. Sometimes, you can see something in your peripheral vision, right? If you look directly at it, it disappears. The Vibrational State is a bit like that. It's elusive. And unless we're in a very deep trance state and the Vibrational State is coming on heavy, it can be hard to catch. And remember, strong emotions or hard thoughts can evaporate it an instant. As soon as we begin to bring our rational mind in and overthink it, it's gone. This is why a mindful mindset is vital for mastering the state. It's a bit like you're eating a ripe peach. You don't narrate the fact that you're going to eat and bite into the peach. "Oh, isn't this a smooth peach. It's very ripe. Oh, it looks very juicy. Oh, there's a little bit there." You don't do that, right? You just eat it. So you don't comment on the experience as it's happening. You just bite into it. This is helpful to remember because in the Vibrational State, as soon as logic and reason starts to come in and you narrate too much, this can disperse the state. So stay with the experience, don't overanalyze, and allow it to unfold, and enjoy the ride. This involves using active imagination to effectively kind of fake it before you make it and bring it on. Remember, this will only work if you are deep in the Mind Awake Body Asleep State or the hypnagogic state. But give it a go, and good luck.

What happened next, no one expected. They changed the behavior of the rivers. The wolves had been absent for over 70 years with no natural predator. The deer population rose sharply, and the park's vegetation suffered from overgrazing. While the wolves were few in number, they radically changed the deer's behavior. The deer avoided areas where they risked being trapped in the valleys and gorges. And so the flora in these spots soon started to regenerate. In six years, trees grew five times their normal height, long-departed bird species returned to nest, and the number of grizzly bears increased owing to new abundance of berries on the trees. But what about those rivers? Robert Monroe wrote "Journeys Out of the Body" and founded the Monroe Institute, where the CIA trained astral projection. He was one of the first people to start looking at out-of-body experiences from a more secular viewpoint without the dogma of religion. In his early days, he understood there to be three planes. Locale one, objective reality here and now, the human plane. Locale two, the astral, the spirit world or the afterlife. Locale three, wider dimensions of reality, planetary systems beyond the astral plane. After more research, he realized that these planes were more nuanced and he split the locales into a spectrum of stages that he calls focus levels. For example, focus level 10 is the mind awake body asleep state. Then as we become more practiced, we can enter wider realms of reality. Focus level 15 is a state of no time. Focus level 23 is the place that he says we find ourself in after death. Focus levels 24 and 26 are what's known as belief system territories, places where people with shared beliefs experience the same things such as particular heavenly realms. He categorizes up to 49 levels, but there are infinitely more. These various environments typically correlate to the type of OBEs we can find ourself in. This is true also in terms of how we feel. Have you ever finished watching a horror movie, and then every creak, bump, or rustle in the house can sound eerie. It can make you jump, right? But what's worse is that when the plane lands, your friend will unconsciously seek out threat where there isn't even any and even self-prophecize it into being. The writer Anais Nin named famously said, "We don't see things as they are. We see them as we are." And modern neuroscience is proving her right. Cognitive neuroscientist Anil Seth goes as far to say that our perception of reality is a kind of controlled hallucination determined to a large degree by what we expect and what we predict to be there. But how does all of this apply to astral projection? The same thing can happen with the astral planes, because our mind, our psychology, comes with us. Your personal beliefs can hijack your perception and totally transform what you notice, like the person who's scared of traveling, but it goes even deeper than that. Because the places we have access to are also somewhat dependent on the content of our consciousness. This is what frequency we operate on. This frequency can kind of resonate with what environment we then have access to. For example, people who believe in angels and demons are more likely to meet them because they are resonating on that plane. Robert Monroe called these belief system territories or consensus realities. You can check this out in his book Journeys Out of the Body if you want to find out more, but this is why it's handy to be aware of your own perception when visiting different planes. What I want to do now is to give you some tools that will help you to see more clearly and gain more control during astral travel. Because our sight can sometimes cause all sorts of problems. So first off, some people successfully leave their body but then find that their vision is blurred. Or it's like they're looking through a tunnel or they're even partially or fully blind. Here are three things you can do if this happens. The first is simply demand, "Clarity now." Simply being clear with what you want, and demanding it with energy and expectation, can influence your perception of the environment. The exact phrase doesn't really matter. It's the intention and the energy you put behind it. You could also try saying, "Awareness now." This is William Buhlman's technique. I've done this a few times when I've entered into my room but it's been complete darkness. The lights kind of lift up and phase into view, but sometimes it's still not crystal clear. So you can say, "Make it clearer." If that doesn't work, or if there's still some kind of block to the clarity of your perception, try to simply relax and tune in. Check if you notice any straining in your awareness and see if you can shift from doing to being, a bit like eating the peach, when we were talking about riding the vibrational plane. The second thing you can do is to try and draw energy from your physical body. This can be a bit of a risky strategy since thinking about the body can snap people back to it. So do this one gently. Simply intend to feel into your body, your physical one, and draw energy from it. It might feel like a kind of sucking sensation towards your current location. When you feel the energy coming into you, guide it towards your sense of perception, so where you would imagine your astral eyes to be. You can also use this technique if you feel stuck, heavy, or unable to move. If neither of these techniques work, check to see if you can perceive your environment using a different sense. Most of us in our society favor sight as their predominant way of navigating the world. But actually, some people can't see at all, and so they have to rely on their other senses. One of my students is completely blind, and he managed to have an out-of-body experience. Now he'd been trying for a while. And when he had one, he phoned me up, and he left me a message at four in the morning, going "Jade, Jade! I've had an out-of-body experience!" And I said, well, how did you feel it? How did you sense into it? And it was very much through all of his other senses, but he did manage to see some things. And there's a book by Kenneth Ring called "Mindsight." He did many studies on how blind people are able to have out-of-body experiences and not only how they can see, but how they can sense reality in other ways. Equally, it's worth letting go of expectations. It can seem like a paradox, but being clear with what we want, whilst unattached to getting it, can bring the experiences we want into fruition without forcing it. It's also a really powerful way just to live our lives. After all, we may be limiting what is possible by being too focused on what we think would be good for us. There may be experiences waiting for us out there that are beyond what we could even imagine. You might also find that you lose focus or concentration during the out-of-body experience and end up phasing back to the body or falling asleep. This can arise from doing the technique too passively. If this happens, try practicing at a different time of day when you would be more alert. An afternoon nap works perfectly fine for many people, but you could also try adjusting your position so you're not completely lying flat and you don't fall asleep. It's all a matter of trial and error, finding what works for you. If you're feeling any anxiety or fear during the OBE, do the Metta-Moment to calm yourself down. Remember, this is when we dropped into the heart space and changed from the lane of fear to love. You can then do the RAIN technique. Remember, recognize, accept, investigate, and non-attach. If you leave your physical body but find yourself energetically stuck somewhere such as in a wall, which has happened to me, try shifting your attention from the problem to the solution. Energy follows focus. So if you get too busy thinking about the wall and how stuck you are, you're probably going to stay there for longer. Instead, focus on your desired destination and where you want to go. This is called anchoring awareness. Concentrate on something you can see or an intent that you have. For now, let's say that we can see a garden gate. We're stuck in a wall, and there's a garden, and we can see a gate. Offer up your desire, and instead go with the flow of what is already happening. One time I got stuck half out of my body and half in. This is a useful perspective to take both whilst out of body and in body in our everyday life. Your actions for today: practice the anchoring awareness exercise in your everyday life. LESSON 13: The Wake-Back-to-Bed Method
--------------------
<v ->Welcome back night yogis.</v> Today, I'm going to share a brilliant astral projection hack with you. It's a sure-fire way to accelerate your practice and a very popular tool among astral projectors. In fact, this technique is used in sleep laboratories across the world. It's actually proven to boost your chances of lucid dreaming, the dreams that you know you're dreaming, by about 2000%, and as we know, there are parallels between these two practices. This approach is also a super efficient way to increase your chances of being out of body too. It's called the wake back to bed method and it's dead easy to learn. Why use the wake back to bed method? So we've spoken about the hypnagogic now a few times, the state we experience just before we fall asleep, that transitory drowsy state, often accompanied by dreamlike displays as we drift off. Practicing our beditation after a period of sleep is much easier way to access the hypnagogic highway. So although you can practice at any time of day, the chances of entering the astral plane increases considerably if you try this after you've already had some sleep. This is because your body and mind isn't as tired, and you can enter the hypnagogic more quickly. So how do you do this exactly? It's super easy, and there's a few simple steps. Set your alarm; simply wake up at least two hours earlier than your usual wake up time. So let's say if you wake up at six normally, you would then wake up at four. If you often wake up at eight, you would then wake up at six. Schedule the time however you like, but make sure that it is at least two hours earlier than when you usually wake up. I know this might seem a bit disruptive, but stay with me on this; this technique significantly boosts your chances to astral project so it's well worth the disruption and the effort. Stay mindfully awake then. So when you wake up, for about 30 to 60 minutes, immerse yourself in an activity linked to astral projection. This could be reading a book, writing in your projection diary, meditating on your motivation, rehearsing even your chosen exit, or reviewing your notes from the course so far. It's important that you stay awake, but you're not wired. So avoid screen time; don't go on your phone; don't watch TV. So after about 30 minutes or 60, set your alarm for two or more hours time, whatever time you want to wake up to start your day. Then play the guided audio, and follow the instructions and the practice. It will take you through the three steps, mind awake body asleep state, vibrational state, and exit technique. Remember the tips and tools to prevent staying awake or falling asleep, and put some of these in place before you start the audio such as thinking about the position you're going to lie in and the way that your room's set up. A reminder here that your motivation is so important at this point because apathy is a big killer and can block progress at this stage. So when you are prompted in the audio to bring your intention and motivation to mind, really feel it in your body; it has to be strong, yet not too charged, too enthusiastic, so avoid feelings of tension or forcefulness; just take it easy. So we are going to do the wake back to bed method tonight, but you might like to do it at the weekend or when other work commitments and responsibilities are minimal so that the following day you've got a lie-in. For future practice, try setting aside one night a week to give this technique a go. Treat it like your astral projection date night with yourself. Don't forget to set your alarm two hours earlier. You might like to have a nightlight on in your room, not too bright so that it will keep you awake, but just very low, like a soft glow in the corner of the room. Some people find this comforting; others find that it stops them from falling asleep completely, so it kind of works for keeping them on that cusp, but it could be too distracting for you, and you might prefer the darkness. Do which you think would be best for you. You might like to consider buddying up with a friend, so you do the wake back to bed method together on the same night as each other. This peer support can add an extra layer of motivation and commitment. Plus, it's a fun thing to do with your friend or partner. Even if you live in separate houses, you can still get up at the same time and do the practice. Then in the morning, you can ring each other up and share your experiences. Decide what your immersive activity will be, and by your bed, have your projection diary ready and waiting just in case you need it. Your actions for today: practice the wake back to bed method with the guided audio. This is in the early morning, so prepare everything you need the night before: your audio, cushions, your projection diary, or any notes you need. Tomorrow, we will finish the week reviewing everything we've learnt so far as well as give you some additional option practice time. In the meantime, good luck, and I will see you on the other side.

LESSON 14: Summary of Your Second Week
--------------------
<v ->Well done on completing week two.</v> We have now learned the three fundamental steps to self-induce an out-of-body experience. These are the mind awake body asleep state, the vibrational state, and exiting the body. Not only that, but we've learned how to approach different planes, navigate the multiverse, and gain more clarity and control, if needed. We've begun to tune into different states, train new habits, and fill our toolbox with different techniques. Now it's a case of trial and error, finding the right method that works for us, and honing our skills. Practice, practice, practice. As part of practice, we need to balance work with play. Otherwise, the mind can become too clingy, too rigid and grasping, for the OBE to happen, which can generate some tension within our consciousness and cause a bit of a roadblock. To soften this straining and free friction from our mind, I'd like you to do an awe-walk today. Awe is one of the most commonly reported emotions felt during astral projection. It's associated with the gamma brainwave, heightened levels of focus, and it expands perspective. It creates an opening in consciousness for wider possibilities. Plus, it's scientifically proven to increase well-being, so win-win all 'round. Awe can be defined as an overwhelming feeling of reverence mixed with fear and wonder. It's often produced by an experience in nature, of which feels vast and mysterious, sacred, sublime, or beyond our conceptual understanding. You might have felt it holding a newborn baby, or watching someone complete a marathon, visiting a beautiful landscape, or staring out at the vastness of the ocean or the starry night sky. In these experiences, we often feel small in the grand scheme of things, and it's this that connects us to something larger. There's a tremendous openness and freedom that comes when you consider yourself a speck of dust in the middle of the universe, or a grain of sand on an expansive beach. You don't stand in the way of anything. You don't overcrowd or obstruct yourself. Instead of trying to be all that, you're humbled by the spaciousness and the smallness. Yet at the same time, you feel bigger than life. Studies show that in an awe state, you feel the presence of something larger than you. You're engaged with the expansiveness of the external world, focused less on yourself and more on others which takes your mind off burdens, trials and tribulations, your worries, anxieties, and frustrations. Whilst these kind of macro-awe experiences can be very powerful, micro-awe is something that we can mindfully cultivate into our normal lives. So let's make every day awe-some. Here's how we can do it. Normally, if someone does an awe-walk, you would go to somewhere awe-inspiring, such as forest, a desert, a beach, or a huge mountain, and I encourage you to definitely do that. But we're going to aim to see awe in the everyday. So I'd like you to go to a garden, a park, a cafe, maybe a busy street, or even when you ride public transport. I'd like you to turn off your phone and tune your awareness outwards into your environment. Watch people walk by. Become aware of the details in things. Maybe pick an area in a garden or a cafe, and look at the intricacies of things such as leaves or the patterns in coffee. Dedicate at least 10 minutes to mindfully observing your senses, and notice how you feel in your body in that moment. Awe often starts as a subtle feeling around your bellybutton. If you pay attention to it, mindfully, you can expand and deepen this sensation. It's a bit like a meditation practice. But bring attention to what seduces your curiosity and attracts your senses outwardly. This could be the symmetrical patterns of colorful flowers, the fractal branching shapes of large trees, the perceptual vastness of the distant horizon, or the golden light after a sunrise or before sunset. The feel and the flow of the breeze or the symphony of bird songs. Even the rain falling on your face, hundreds of feet from the sky. The laughter of children playing, or the power of engines making machines work, or the hustle and bustle of many people on their day's journey. Set an intention to let go of the analytical mind's compulsive labeling of things, and explore more how your environment makes you feel by observing the felt presence in your body. When we ground ourselves in this sense of feeling and aliveness in our bodies, we can awaken a childlike sense of wonder, a mystery of all that we don't know and understand, rather than focusing on what we think we already know. These awe-walks can be powerful experiences for relaxing the mind and helping our bodies recharge. In fact, there's a lot of research showing that cultivating awe and a childlike sense of wonder and curiosity can improve our mood and make us feel more satisfied with life. It can decrease our rumination by making us feel smaller and more humble. It can expand our perception of time, make us feel less rushed, can restore our attention span, and enhance our creative thinking. It can also increase pro-social behaviors, like generosity and kindness. You also begin to notice all sorts of little miracles around you, like how bumblebees can fly. They shouldn't be able to do it! Their bums are too big, and their wings are too small! When I first noticed this, I looked up a picture, and it made me laugh so much. Aerodynamically, they shouldn't be able to fly, but they can! They're like a flying beach ball! So your action for today is to connect to a sense of childlike wonder through doing a 10 minute awe-walk. Of course, it can be longer if you really want to go for it. And of course, keep practicing the techniques we've learnt so far, whichever ones you feel you'd need a bit more practice with, and I'll see you next week.

LESSON 16: 3 Steps to Transform Sleep Paralysis Into Astral Projection
--------------------
<v ->Hello, and welcome back.</v> Today, we are going to talk about a phenomena related to sleep that you might encounter: sleep paralysis. We're going to look at how to transform it into astral projection. You wake up in the middle of the night and feel a pressure on your chest and a feeling of fear in your heart. You try to move, but your limbs will not budge. You try to call out, but no sound comes out. It's as though you're partially awake but somehow stuck in sleep. Everything seems so real, and you ask yourself, is this a bad dream? This might sound like a nightmare, and in many ways it is, but what you might be experiencing is sleep paralysis. For many, this strange occurrence of feeling half asleep and half awake, not being able to move, locked in your body, can be a frightening experience. However, if armed with a couple of simple approaches you can not only overcome this phenomenon but you can also harness it as a way to experience the out-of-body state. For the record, astral projection does not cause sleep paralysis, but as astral travelers, we can certainly use it to our advantage. Firstly, what is sleep paralysis? It's important to understand why sleep paralysis happens. When you understand this process, it will help you to overcome it, should you ever encounter it. The reason you can't move or speak is because your body is fast asleep. Most likely in REM, rapid eye movement dream sleep. During REM sleep, your physical body can't move. It's a protective measure the brain uses, so you don't move or act out your dreams, or fall out of bed, or wander outside. Although your body is asleep, your brain has partially woken up, and your senses are taking in some sensory input. This means your mind is half awake. You can sense some things from the outside world, but your physical body cannot move. And sometimes because you're half in a dream and half awake, you might see pictures or scenes playing out in front of you. It's almost as if there are images superimposed over your normal bedroom scene. There may even be some sounds that you might hear. The fear that this altered state generates can also lead to hyperventilation and in turn, a feeling of a weight on the chest. However, rest assured sleep paralysis is more common than you might think. Around 40% of people have experienced it to some degree before. When can it occur then? It can happen at any point during your night's sleep, but sleep paralysis is most commonly occurring during the hypnopompic, the transitional state of waking up out of sleep and dream. But sometimes it can occur in the hypnagogic too. For many people, this phenomenon of partially waking up from sleep, but the body remaining paralyzed, can be terrifying in which they get hallucinatory images and sounds that may lead them to believe that demons are trying to possess them. So now, it's a good time for some myth-busting with this. Firstly, rest assured, sleep paralysis isn't anything external, such as a demon or a spirit, though it can be really scary. But we've just discovered that it's simply a mechanism of the brain. Astral projection doesn't cause sleep paralysis. Sleep paralysis and astral projection are not the same thing. They're two different phenomena with different attributes and sensations, two different states of consciousness. Although our natural response is to fight sleep paralysis, actually, the harder you struggle to move, the less likely you are to wake up out of it. Lastly, the great thing is is that you can harness sleep paralysis to enter an out-of-body experience. So if that's the myth, then what's the reality? The reality is that sleep paralysis is a natural phenomena that we need not fear, and can instead utilize for our astral projection practice. I've experienced it a lot over the years, and depending on my level of awareness, how clear I am in my mind at the time and also my skill at that time as an astral projector, depends on how I deal with it and what happens afterwards. Here's an example. One night, I woke up in sleep paralysis. I was lying on my back with my head turned towards the window. I could not move my body or speak, and my eyes were open. So sometimes you can have your eyes open and still see dream imagery overlaid over your room at the same time. My gaze was fixed in the direction that my body was laying. All of a sudden, the curtain morphed into a hooded figure. It looked like the Ringwraith from Lord of the Rings or the Death Eaters from Harry Potter. It turned to face me menacingly. Instantly, I did the Metta-Moment, where we drop into the heart space and we bring ourselves to a place of gratitude. The hallucination vanished. Then all of a sudden, straight after, a giant spider from the ceiling dropped down towards my face. I'm scared of spiders. Again, I took a Metta-Moment, and before the spider landed on my face, it dissolved away. This is what I call neutralizing the space during sleep paralysis. We have the power to influence what is happening, but only when we control our emotions. Because our emotions affect the hallucinations. If you're full of fear and panic, guess what is going to happen? You're going to manifest a personification of those feelings. So what do we do if we find ourselves in sleep paralysis? Here are three options. One, the prevention and the release of sleep paralysis. To prevent episodes before they happen, avoid anything that might disrupt your usual sleep routine, and avoid sleeping on your back. It's often the fear of this altered state that can lead to the fast breathing and sometimes a feeling of a weight on the chest. However, there are some other simple ways to overcome sleep paralysis once you're in it. If you want to snap out of it, try this nifty breathing technique. Relax, and exhale through your front teeth, making a sound similar to letting air out of a tire. It's a little bit like whistling through your teeth like this. Let's try it together now. See if you can go longer than me when you do it. Okay, deep breath in, and keep going as long as you can. If you're still going, keep with it, keep with it, keep with it. Okay, maybe you're still going; well done. This will help to disengage the sleep paralysis mechanism and bring you out of it. The key is to relax and stay calm. Easier said than done, right? But you can do it. And once you've done that, it's recognizing that it's not a threatening situation or nightmare. There's nothing to fear, and you will wake up at any moment. You're safe, and this will pass. Two, use it as a gateway to astral project. If you're feeling brave, you can alchemize sleep paralysis into a gateway for astral projection. The good thing is you already know a couple of skills to help make this happen. Here's how to do it. Try to stay in sleep paralysis instead of resisting and fighting it. So we're going to learn an affirmation that we can use in that moment where we're feeling overwhelmed with emotions. The affirmation is, "I release control; I surrender to the flow." "I release control; I surrender to the flow." If you say this with feeling, so genuinely feel that surrender, and offer it up to that moment, it should be able to help disengage that resistance and that fight or flight that you feel yourself in. You can back this up with RAIN technique. Remember, recognize what's happening. Okay, I'm in sleep paralysis. Accept that you're here. Okay, accept I'm in sleep paralysis. Investigate, what is in this space? What can I see or sense around me? And non-identification. Don't attach a story to your surroundings. Oh my God, I'm going to get possessed by a demon, attacked by a negative entity. This is just a story that's going to send us into a negative thought spiral. Then if during this process, you notice more scary hallucinations, or perhaps you don't see anything at all, but you sense a negative presence, you can take a Metta-Moment, dropping into that feeling of loving kindness and gratitude, just like I did. This will neutralize the space. Remember, this is dropping into the heart space and connecting with feelings of love, gratitude, and compassion which can help shift our psyche from fear to love. Alternatively, if you have a strong association with a spiritual practice such as prayer or mantra, you could use this instead, especially if it means a lot to you. In some cases, this might even work better than the Metta-Moment because it holds a special place in your heart, and it's more familiar for you to do it in that moment. LESSON 18: Changing Planes: Lucid Dream to Astral Projection
--------------------
<v ->Hello, astral travelers.</v> Today, we're going to talk about how we can enter the astral plane through secret doors, specifically, how we can use a lucid dream as a gateway to an out-of-body experience. On one hand, you could call this a shortcut. On another, it's a bit like trying to get through the front doors of Buckingham Palace. It's dependent on how easily and often you lucid dream. Let me explain. Firstly, what is a lucid dream? Well, it's not a vivid dream. It's not an out-of-body experience. A lucid dream is effectively a dream in which we know we are dreaming, and we're able to exert some influence over the environment. Humans have been doing this for many years. It's only been recently though, that we've realized that you can actually do some pretty powerful inner growth work with lucid dreams, including entering the astral plane. In sleep labs across the world, it's been proven that one of the best ways to evoke a lucid dream is to use the wake back to bed method. Researchers in labs found that two-thirds of their participants experienced a lucid dream after using the wake back to bed method. So although the wake back to bed method is a great tool for astral projectors, it's also an excellent tool for lucid dreamers, making lucid dreams a happy bonus and just one positive side effect from this wake back to bed method. How to check whether you are lucid dreaming. Reality checks. Lucid dreaming can feel very lifelike at times, so it's important to test whether you are dreaming or not. In a dream, to test whether or not you are actually in one, you can perform a reality check. Here's how to do it. You look at your hand, you look away, and you look back. When you look back at your hands, they will be blurry or misshapen or growing a tree. Something weird will be happening. And this is because the mind can't replicate the same image twice in quick succession. Or try to switch on a light switch on the wall. Your brain won't be able to make the light appear as quickly as you press the switch. You can also try to read the text on your mobile phone or screen in a dream. You'll find that the words are illegible. They might be jumping around or difficult to read. So what are the differences and similarities between astral projection and lucid dreaming? People often report that having an out-of-body experience feels realer than real. It feels way more than a very vivid dream. The difference is that you have the sensation of separating from the body, the exit, and you know that you're not dreaming. You have a profound gnosis that it's definitely not a dream. It can feel a little surreal and yet can be profoundly exhilarating. You can see why lucid dreaming and astral projection are sometimes mixed up, 'cause lucid dreaming can feel very real as well. The onset of an OBE is characterized by a distinctive physical sensation, this moving beyond. It can include the vibrational state. So we don't have the vibrational state before you went to a lucid dream; you just suddenly know you're in a dream. But with astral projection, a lot of people pass through the vibrational state. Two, connection to your body. In an OBE, you suddenly become aware that your consciousness seems to be outside of your body. Remember, you can turn back and look at it lying there. And don't forget, we learned about the two different bodies, the difference between the dream body and the energy body; they feel and look very different. Also in a lucid dream, you know that you're in a dream, you typically accept, oh, I'm dreaming. So subjectively, the experiences are different, and you're still connected to your body because that just feels like a given. Three, awareness of the physical world. Whereas a lucid dream, you arrive in the dream itself, and you're within 360 degrees of your own psychology that feels incredibly real. So in a lucid dream, you can change the environment because it's your own psyche, a bit like a video game, where you can build different villages and influence different things. In an OBE, you can't really do that, because we are entering into objective realities or other dimensions that are interacting with our own psyche, but are not fully 100% a part of it. So this is why the environments might be different. So this is also why the call and response doesn't really work in the same way. So what I mean by call and response, is in a lucid dream you could call out as I suggested, and then something would change in response to it. LESSON 20: Wake-Back-To-Bed: Create Your Own Ganzfeld Experiment
--------------------
<v ->Today, I'm going to teach you a technique</v> on how to tune in and strengthen your polyphasic perception. This is the same type of perception that we're honing for our astral eyes. Polyphasic perception is ways of knowing information other than through the five senses. You might like to think of it as extrasensory perception or perhaps even a sort of psychic ability. The Ganzfeld experiment tests a person's extrasensory abilities such as intuition, telepathy, psychometry, and clairvoyance, and precognition. It helps one to tune in to what's called a sixth sense or a second sight. The power to perceive things that are not present to the five senses but whereby a person can perceive information in the form of a vision, a future event, things before they happen, or at a remote location, such as remote viewing. This not only helps us to develop these abilities for and within astral projection, but if we get into the Mind Awake Body Asleep State during the experiment, we can harness the Ganzfeld effect to springboard into an OBE. It was first used by Charles Honorton when investigating telepathy in waking and dreaming states at the Maimonides Medical Center in New York. The procedure involved placing the participant, who was called the receiver, in a chair and inducing a state of reduced sensory input. This is believed to remove the sensory noise of everyday life which may mask or weaken the telepathy signal. This state is achieved by covering the participant's eyes with halved ping pong balls, with a red light shining on them to create a homogenized visual field, as well as playing white noise through a headset at the same time. The sender, a participant in another room, or in some cases, the computer in the autoganzfeld studies, is given a randomly selected target picture which they attempt to transmit to the receiver. The receiver is asked to describe any images that they might see within their awareness. The receiver's description is then compared to the target. And this is usually independent by a panel of judges who don't know about the experiment's objectives or the target. Now, we aren't going to do this specific experiment. I just wanted to give you an idea of how it's been used in the past so you can see how it works. But what we are going to do is create our own Ganzfeld experiment and see if we can launch into the astral planes from there. This is pretty exciting. Okay, here's what you need to do it: a ping pong ball, tape, a bright solid light that can flood the whole room, your face as much as possible. Otherwise, it won't work. Headphones, preferably noise-canceling ones, and an uninterrupted static white noise. So you can use the audio track for this. So what do we need to do? We want to cut the ping pong ball in half; shape the half balls to our face so that it covers the eyes without leaving any gaps around the edges of our visual field. You don't want to see any of your room. This is really important. Then we want to turn on the light to fill the room so it's a solid, uniform, bright light. Then, we want to sit and lie down in a comfortable position, just like we would do for our practice. Then we put the headphones on, and we play the static white noise. We want to cover each eye with a ping pong ball and hold it in place with tape. From here, it's just a case of relaxing. So you might like to do the 4-7-8 breath, the tension exercise, or anything you can do to relax. After a short amount of time, sights and sounds and perceptions might arise as your mind starts to fill in the blank space of the uniform sensory field, AKA create hallucinations, similar to the hypnagogic and hypnopompic imagery. In fact, you might find that this is even more vivid than those states. Then, I'd like you to do an exit technique to springboard from this state into astral projection. We're going to look at how to do therapeutic tremoring. Therapeutic tremoring is also known as shaking therapy. It's a phrase coined by Dr. David Berceli. This involves shaking the body to release tension and trauma. It helps to regulate the nervous system. Have you ever seen a dog or a cat shake something off? Rainwater, a buildup of stress after a cat fight, or being prodded by the vet. They shake the tip of their nose to the end of their tail and almost immediately recover from something physically or emotionally uncomfortable. You might have seen this in a nature documentary where the lion is hunting the antelope. It escapes, and then it shudders afterwards, releasing the stress of the chase. We too, like all animals, have the ability to do this. We shake involuntary after intense experiences, like being in an accident, giving birth, or public speaking. And we often tell people to stop shaking, but it's the shaking it off that is actually a valid thing to do for your nervous system. We've been socially conditioned to grin and bear it. But this isn't natural, and it traps the stress in our bodies. And this can impact our health in the long term. Trauma expert, Steve Haines, explains, "We don't shake because we're traumatized, we shake as a response." It's a very primitive mechanism to reset muscle tension from a stuck state to release stress and to enhance the mind-body connection. Effectively, it encourages the body to return back to a state of balance. We're going to learn how to do this for two purposes in astral projection. The first is called the exhaustion method. LESSON 22: Encountering Other Travelers & Meeting Ancestors
--------------------
<v ->Welcome back travelers.</v> Did you shake it off? I hope so. If you haven't had a full-blown OBE yet, don't worry. Remember it's considered a siddha, a superpower, in many spiritual traditions. So it takes time. In fact, it took me four weeks of practice before I had my first adult one, and it took William Buhlman, the lead trainer at the Monroe Institute, a month too. So you are on the right track. Stick with it, and don't forget, you're on the hero's journey. When visiting the astral planes, there are all sorts of beings we can encounter. What we think these entities are is very much dependent on our own belief system which is often the religion we were brought up in or what our parents or school taught us. Some people believe these beings to be spirits. Others think they're part of our own mind. From my experience, it's not that black and white. We still don't really know the depth of how consciousness and our reality interact with each other. It's a great mystery. But what we do know, in regards to astral projection, is that we can seem to enter objective environments, our reality here and now, and subjective environments made entirely from our own mind, and intersubjective environments. These consensus realities, where people with shared belief systems access the same planes and even meet each other. From my trips to the Astral, there certainly seems to be a broad spectrum between the places we visit and the beings we encounter. A bit like the animal kingdom; there are many lands with all sorts of beasts who have different degrees of intelligence and self-awareness. From monkeys to jellyfish and elephants to ladybugs, all sorts of beautiful creatures. We can be afraid of them and stay in the house or we can be curious and go on astral safari. Let's look at the types of encounters that you might have so you know what to expect. Are you ready for your astral safari? You might meet a thought-form. The most common type of encounter is meeting a thought-form. Thought-forms can seem like other beings. In fact, they're often mistaken for spirits separate to ourselves. These types of entities are created purely by thought. They are personified aspects of our own mind. Now, it can be confusing because they seem to have some self-autonomy. In the same way a zombie looks alive and make sounds and is driven by primal instinct, the same can be said for thought-forms. It's a projected thought made real. They can take on their own independent reality and can even behave in very surprising and spontaneous ways but are nonetheless generated by an individual or even a collective group. This is how consensus realities are created. Think of it this way. When we dream, we meet thought-forms all the time. In our dreams, the characters are us, and we can have chats with them. They go about their day-to-day activities, operating on their own terms, right? Sometimes they're friendly and have exciting messages. Other times they're scary and have urgent warnings. If we meet a thought-form in the astral, we can do the RAIN technique, but instead of doing it with the environment, we can do it with the thought-form. So, we'd recognize what it is and maybe tune in to see if we can get a sense of its energy. What does it want? What does it need? Accept its presence in the space with us; allow it to be there, and investigate; ask it questions. Who are you? Do you have a message for me? And then non-identify; don't start spinning stories in your mind about the thought-form, but instead, be open to what it has to say. Often, they can be unintegrated parts of our shadow, parts of ourselves we've pushed away, but more on that tomorrow. You might meet helpers or intruders. From time to time, we might find ourselves out of body and know that there's someone with us. Occasionally, we can see this presence, but a lot of the time we just might feel it. We might sense it's in the same space, or it could even be right beside us like a companion. These are called intruders and helpers. Helpers appear like positive guides nudging us in the right direction. Intruders appear like negative strangers encroaching on our space. They can appear threatening, but often intruders are just a shadow thought-form. A part of ourself we've pushed away, that wants to be integrated, but we'll look at the shadow tomorrow. During these moments, we get a sense that we're being told or shown something or guided to go somewhere. We can choose whether or not we engage and interact with them, or we could go on our own journeys. If I had a penny for every time a friend told me they astral-projected out of their body but then felt a presence and got too scared and shot back into their body, I'd be a pretty rich woman. This is why overcoming fears and limiting beliefs is so important. You don't want to miss a special opportunity because you got scared. If you sense someone is with you, turn towards whoever it is and tune in using your intuition to read why they might be with you. You know when you have a chat with a friend and you read between the lines of what they're saying, when you sense into what they really want to say behind the words, it's a bit like that. So be calm and open and receptive. If you want to leave, you can choose at any time to go to a different place or back to your body. Many beginners are passive. They just accept and go with the circumstance that they find themselves in. Don't forget: you have the power; you have power to control what you do and where you go. So you can do whatever you wish. Don't forget that. Communication in the astral is usually telepathic. Like you just know each other's intentions. In non-physical realities, information can come as an intuitive knowing, a sort of energy ball of information. What Robert Monroe called a ROTE which is a Related Organized Thought Energy. Basically, it's a download that's instantaneously transmissible from one person to another. It might take you a while to get used to this, but if you meet a being, it usually happens without much effort. You just seem to know how to do it, like it's natural. The key to this communication is to be clear, to be open to receiving information, however that comes. Not thinking that you have to receive it just through a visual or an auditory way, but rather it's like an intuitive wave of data. Of course you might see and hear things too. For example, you might be taken to see something, or you might hear a message, but often the language is intuitive. You also might meet someone who's passed over. When I met my dead father during an out-of-body experience, his message was communicated through knowing, feeling, and words. I had entered into this beautiful garden, and he appeared from behind a fountain, and he was so happy to see me. I couldn't believe it was happening. It was so unexpected, and we ran to each other and embraced. And when I touched him, I shrunk down into my four-year-old self, which was completely unexpected, and I was just so overwhelmed with emotion. And he bent down on one knee, the way you do when you're with a child, and he looked me in the eye, and he said, "I'm so sorry. I didn't know. I didn't know." You see, I had a dysfunctional relationship with my father in my life, and his behavior hugely impacted me in a negative way which he didn't realize at the time. Somehow he knew that, and there was this wonderful exchange of love and forgiveness. And then he took my hand, and he led me to a huge door which he pushed open into a great hall. And he said, "Look where I've been!" And there were all these people dancing everywhere. My dad loved to dance, and he took my hand, and he pulled me through the crowds like he used to do when I was a little girl, and everyone was so joyful, smiling at me. And then the journey continued on. And at the end of that, he waved me goodbye from a mountain top as I returned back to my body. That remains to be one of the most beautiful experiences I've ever had. And when I came back from it, it felt as though a weight had been lifted. I couldn't believe that I'd got to see him one last time. And it helped me heal the grief that I've been holding on for for so long. It is possible to encounter your own loved ones and others that have died, in the astral planes. And in some traditions, they use astral travel to help people move on in after-death states. So we not only have the power to connect to our own ancestors, but also, we can help others. If you would like to connect with a loved one in an OBE, you might like to do this exercise to call them in and to connect with them in the astral. Step one, create a new projection plan focused on meeting your loved one who has passed away. For example, "I call on my ancestors to help me go beyond the body to meet my dead father for the purpose of healing grief." You can change the words to make it more personal for you. Step two, find a quiet place where you can do this meditation. If you have a space that you meditate in or a favorite spot, you could do it there. Just make sure you feel comfortable. Then, light a candle in acknowledgement of the person who has passed and give them an offering. An offering is something to honor them, maybe something you know they'd like: it could be a flower, their favorite chocolate, you could even play a piece of music that they love. When I did this recently for my grandma, I gave her a cup of tea because she used to go through about 10 cups a day. So choose what you think is best. Step three, then, hold or look at a photo of them and bring them into your heart. Call them into your awareness. Do this in whatever way feels right for you. It could be through a feeling, through words, or a picture in your mind. Step four, then, do your astral practice as normal. And when you find yourself in the mind awake body asleep state, remind yourself of your projection plan; say it, then continue with the exercises that you've chosen for that specific practice to self-initiate an OBE. Step five, when you leave the body, you might already find yourself being taken to where you need to go. Whoever you have called in might even be with you right away. But if you find yourself in your room, call out to your loved one in the same way that you did in the meditation. Then, back this up with a command to be taken to where they are. Dropping into the feeling of why you want to meet them is a really good thing to do at the same time in that moment. Remember, it's a thought-responsive environment. So don't forget to release attachment to any outcome. Once you've done the practices, let go of any expectations, and then be open to whatever happens. A reminder that the non-physical planes don't always operate on the same linear timeframe that we experience from day to day. You could do this practice, and then the OBE might spontaneously happen five days later. It doesn't always occur that night or unfold in the way we expect. Some traditions believe that the soul, the person, may be on their own evolutionary journey. So if you don't get an immediate response, don't be disheartened, and look out for their presence or message in other experiences such as dreams. People have also had visitation dreams from a dead relative after this practice. Lastly, doing this can be quite emotional. So allow any feelings to come up and express themselves in whichever way they arise, and then maybe write them down in your diary. Good luck. And I'll see you tomorrow.

LESSON 23: The Descent: Soul Retrieval & Shadow Integration
--------------------
<v ->Hello, dear night yogis.</v> I've mentioned that astral projection can be used as a spiritual tool for healing and elevating consciousness. Today, we're going to learn how to integrate pieces of our own soul and our shadow, the parts of us that are separated from ourself and in the shadows, back in again. This is because we might manifest and even meet this side of ourselves in our astral journeys. One of the ways in which we're going to do this is through soul retrieval. The word shaman comes from the Tungus tribe in Siberia, and it means one who sees in the dark. Shamanism has been practiced in parts of Asia, Europe, Africa, Australia, Greenland, and native North and South America. In her book, Soul Retrieval, Sandra Ingerman explains that a shaman is a man or a woman who interacts directly with spirits or elemental energies to address the spiritual aspects of illness, divine information, and help the spirits of dead people cross over. Also to perform a variety of ceremonies for their community, including something called soul retrieval. The term soul retrieval is usually used to describe the process of reintegrating aspects of the self that have somehow become split off. This splitting off, or fracturing, often occurs due to trauma, whether it's in this lifetime or a previous one, and it can lead to fragments of the self being kind of stuck in different times, realities, or in simply different parts of our psyche. Whenever or wherever we experience a heavy trauma, parts of our self or soul may flee or fracture, kind of hide in an effort to protect itself. This is often referred to as soul loss. The trauma that creates this soul loss might be as obvious as an injury, an assault, or war. It could also be from the death of a loved one, a divorce, even physical and emotional abuse. Or it might be seemingly a hidden thing, such as womb trauma, or intergenerational trauma that's been passed on, even past life trauma. Depression, dysfunctional relationships, a sense of separation, inability to move forward, and inherent lack of self-awareness can all be hallmarks of soul loss. And so the task of soul retrieval is to find the parts of our soul and to reclaim them, to reintegrate them back into wholeness of the self. The end goal of which is to fully integrate all aspects of ourselves. Although soul retrieval is often performed by a shaman on our behalf, once we learn astral projection, we can practice soul retrieval for ourselves. In the OBE state, we can become our own shaman. Soul retrieval in OBEs can happen in one of two ways: either the parts of our soul that have split off try to sort of seek us out in the astral, and we might stumble upon them spontaneously, or if we feel ready to do so, we can intentionally invoke them, seek them out, once we are out of body, to then integrate them. In the first option, during an astral projection experience, split-off parts of ourself might appear to us as thought-forms that might seek us out for reintegration. The reason for this might be because the more subtle energetic form that we inhabit in an OBE, so our energy body, is easier to reintegrate with than the physical grosser form of waking life. Or it could be that the ego is somewhat weakened in the OBE state, our sense of self. So we're more open and more able, more flexible, to reassimilate the lost parts of ourselves than in the ego-dominated waking state. Whatever the case, what we know for sure is that this can happen. So let's be prepared for it and be open to the healing that it offers. Sometimes in the OBE state, these fragments of the split-off self or soul may appear as if they were autonomous individuals and crucially, as if they were separate from you. In fact, many of the thought-forms that we encounter in these non-physical realms can often take on multiple manifestations that are seemingly independent to ourselves. A very common response upon meeting these aspects is no, that was definitely not a part of me. This is a totally natural response because these are parts of your soul, your psyche, that are fragmented and split off. And so naturally, they do feel unfamiliar, but because they are already split off, if we then react with fear or aversion, or by pushing them away, they will remain split off, separate, and unintegrated from us. If you can be willing to integrate the energy that they hold though, by facing and embracing them in some way, either through dialogue, showing them love, or even literally embracing them if that feels good for you, then we can have a powerful healing experience. But what about that other option? The one in which you intentionally seek out lost parts of your soul to reintegrate. For this, you make it a part of your projection plan. You simply make it part of your purpose and intention. Can you remember when we wrote in our projection diary in week one, our meaningful motivation and our intention, what we wanted to do. This is where you can add in the purpose of soul retrieval as part of your plan. You might want to write down, "I call on my highest self to help me go beyond the body, to unify my whole self for the purpose of soul retrieval." We can also integrate our shadow. Just as we may encounter split parts of our soul, our psyche, in an OBE, we might also be able to encounter unintegrated aspects of our shadow too. So, what is the shadow, and what is the protocol for if we encounter it in our astral travel? The shadow is the part of ourself that is made up of all we hide from. And all that has been split off from who we think we are, our shame, our fears, our wounds, but also our divine spirit, our blinding beauty, and our hidden talents. The concept of the shadow is found within most cultures and spiritual traditions all over the world, but it was first popularized in the West by the legendary Swiss psychiatrist, Carl Jung. He used it to describe the part of the unconscious mind that was made up of all the seemingly undesirable aspect of the psyche, ourselves. The shadow is our dark side, but not dark as in negative or malign, but rather dark as in not yet illuminated. It consists of everything within us that we don't want to face and that has become split off. That is everything both seemingly harmful and potentially enlightening. All that we've rejected, denied, disowned, or repressed. So the shadow is not evil or bad. It is simply the parts of ourself that seem incompatible with who we think we are. These might include our shame, our fears, our emotional wounds, but also crucially, our awakened essence, our unexpressed talents, and our highest potential. Shadow integration involves shining light into the dark caves of our minds to reintegrate the split-off traumatized parts of ourselves. Any spiritual path that aspires to psychological wholeness will incorporate shadow integration to some degree, simply because unless the shadow is integrated, made whole, the mind remains divided. Any of this sound familiar? Reintegration of split-off parts of ourself, traumatized aspects that we unconsciously hide in the shadows of our minds. Although soul retrieval and shadow integration aren't exactly the same, they are quite similar. And so the same face and embrace advice goes for both. So if you meet a shadow aspect in the astral which, just like a lost-soul part, may well appear as an independent energy that seems separate from you, you know what to do. Accept it, show it love, send it positive energy, or do whatever feels right for you in that moment. And that might even feel like embracing it, giving it a hug. How will you know what's your shadow, and what isn't? If we look at dreams, anything that is in the dream that makes us feel scared, so even to the point of maybe being disgusted, or repulsed, or petrified, it could be our shadow. Or it might be something we are absolutely dazzled by, we're in awe of, a blinding brilliance, our divinity: that is your shadow. It can take a bit of time to build intuition, and one way of doing that is getting to know ourselves in the waking state, so we can sense into what could be shadow, and what might not be, but those are some good signs to see whether it might be. Once you see any shadow aspect, go towards it; you'll want to run away, but see if you can have the courage to move in its direction. Interact with it, dialogue with it, ask it what its name is. What does it represent? What message or insight does it have for you? And if you feel called to, maybe even see if you can hug it with fearless compassion. All this, embracing split-off shadow aspects, and reintegrating traumatized parts of our soul can sound pretty intense, right? If you're afraid in the OBE, when it's actually happening, remember you can take a metta-moment. Step back into your heart space, and remind yourself of the crucial truth. You can never be harmed in a non-physical environment because there's simply nothing to attack. There's no body or no thing that can be harmed. You are made of energy, not matter. And remember, this is a part of yourself. It wants to be integrated; it wants to be seen. So see it. And don't forget that the astral is a thought-responsive environment. And so if we take our fear into a thought-responsive environment, then that fear may be instantly projected and reflected back to us as an embodied part of what we fear. In the astral, it is our fear that creates fearful experiences, much more than anything else being objective to be afraid of. And remember, your beliefs are often reflected in the frequency of the realms you have access to. As Luigi Sciambarella from the Monroe Institute says, "Remember, many who have ventured into these territories before you haven't been harmed. And that actually what is coming to confront you is just a part of you that wants to be integrated. If only you could move beyond the fear and judgment that may prevent that." One thing we can do to help with healing our soul and shadow parts is a practice called Ho'oponopono. Ho'oponopono is a beautiful practice. It's one of my favorites. It's a Hawaiian forgiveness practice that allows us to create new connections and rejuvenate our relationship with the shadow, or those soul parts of ourself that are split off. In Huna, the ancient Hawaiian discipline of energy and healing, the Ho'oponopono process is essential if we want to be Pono, right and congruent with ourselves. The Hawaiian word Ho'oponopono comes from Ho, to make, and Pono, right, to make right. The repetition of the word Pono means doubly right, or being right with both ourselves and others. In a nutshell, Ho'oponopono is a process by which we can forgive ourselves and others that may have contributed in some way to soul loss and our shadow. Forgiving ourselves and others for anything we did or didn't do in the moment when the soul loss occurred, or when the shadow was formed, is a very powerful thing to do in the astral plane. It has a profound healing impact. Here's how to do it. Okay, let's say in the astral planes, you are faced with your shadow self or in an environment where you sense soul loss. What do you do? This is what you do. You say and feel these words as deeply as possible. "I'm sorry, please forgive me. Thank you. I love you." "I'm sorry, please forgive me. Thank you. I love you." And then just be open to whatever might happen afterwards. This is a very, very powerful practice, and it's not limited to astral projection. You can also do this in other altered states, such as meditation or dreamwork. Your actions for today: your action for today is to listen to the guided shamanic journey.
