LESSON 24: The Final Flight: Conscious Dying
--------------------
<v ->Welcome back, everyone.</v> I'm going to give it to you straight: today is going to be challenging. It's not going to be easy, but it will be very insightful, possibly one of the most beneficial days we've had so far. This is because I want to talk about something that most of us naturally turn a blind eye to. I want to talk about death. While we are alive, we have a wonderful opportunity to prepare ourselves for death and dying. And that starts by being willing to have a conversation about it. And having an out-of-body experience can help overcome the fear of death even further. So today, we will be focusing on the Tibetan Buddhist teachings and how astral projection offers the opportunity for enlightenment upon death. My former husband and lucid dreaming teacher, Charlie Morley, often says, death is not a swear word, because in today's society, the word "death" has become pathologized into an almost dirty word. In Charlie's book, "Dreaming Through Darkness," he notes how each day, 150,000 people die and that of course, one day you and I will do too. But he asks, when was the last time you reflected on the fact that you're going to die? In the West, most of us live for about 1000 months, but of those 1000 months, how long do we spend preparing for everything that those 1000 months have been leading up to? Death is the greatest equalizer, a shared commonality of human experience, a natural part of life. We will all die, definitely, and successfully, and yet, we never really prepare for it, and we hardly ever talk about it, but why is that? Fear, mostly, but also denial, suppression, and shame. Death is for many people the greatest fear, and so transmutation of this fear can reap the greatest benefits. We need to begin readdressing this imbalance and start waking up to the reality of our own mortality. Talking about death shouldn't be taboo, but it kind of still is. Anthropologist Ernest Becker wrote in his Pulitzer Prize-winning book, "The Denial of Death," that Sigmund Freud was wrong and that, "It is death, not sex, that is the primary suppression of mankind." If this is true, then we can see why it might be a sensitive subject to broach. The interesting thing is awareness of our mortality can actually improve our physical health and help us reprioritize our goals and values. Even nonconscious thinking about death, such as walking by a cemetery, can prompt positive change and promote helping others. As an example of how awareness of death can be of benefit is the work of Bronnie Ware. Bronnie Ware is an Australian nurse who spent several years working in palliative care, looking after other patients in the last 12 weeks of their lives. She recorded their dying epiphanies and noticed the same five recurring themes. She put these revelations into a book called "The Five Regrets of the Dying." This is what the five regrets are. Number one, I wish I'd had the courage to live a life true to myself, not the life others expected of me. Number two, I wish I'd had the courage to express my feelings. Three, I wish I'd stayed in touch with my friends. Four, I wish I had let myself be happier. Five, I wish I hadn't worked so hard. When people first hear about the Five Regrets, it often inspires them to contact that friend they lost touch with, go for that new job, share their feelings, or start a creative hobby, or simply just take the pressure off themselves and say, this is where I'm at right now, and that's okay. So paradoxically, thinking about death can help us live more fully. Granted, this is easier said than done, isn't it? But one of the most direct ways that we can harness this paradoxical benefit is through astral projection. Having an OBE has been scientifically proven to show a radical decrease in death anxiety and to help grief. Almost all people who have an OBE come back convinced that they are not ultimately just their physical body, and in the same way that near-death experiencers return convinced of an afterlife or a spirit world, projectors usually return believing that they have a spirit or a soul or a consciousness that will in some way go on after death. Now, whether or not we personally believe that to be true maybe doesn't matter because either way, the lessening of death anxiety happens, and that can be very comforting to many people. As the American neuroscientist Sam Harris points out, whether or not a person's consciousness can actually be displaced is perhaps irrelevant. The point is, it can seem to be. Dr. Mel Slater's team at Barcelona University showed that even a virtual reality experience mimicking an OBE can decrease the fear of death. As Eckhart Tolle says, the secret to life is to die before you die and to find out that there is no death. This is what many near-death experiencers report. The world's largest near-death experience study was led by Dr. Sam Parnia, a professor at New York Langone Medical Center. It involved 2060 patients from 15 different hospitals in the UK, United States, and Austria. Physicians used the latest technologies to study the brain and consciousness during a cardiac arrest, a heart attack. The clinical timing of death currently in the West is when the brain shuts down and the heart stops. You shouldn't be able to sense or feel anything. However, many people in the study had a spectrum of perception and awareness after this moment had happened. It proved that death isn't a moment, but it's a process. Yet, some traditions have known about this for centuries and use it to die consciously. Dying consciously with awareness is seen as a possibility within both the ancient Mexican shamanic tradition of the Toltec, the Sufi lineages and of the Middle East, and in Tibetan Buddhism. So the idea of death being an opportunity seems to be found cross-culturally. Astral projection, as well as lucid dreaming and conscious sleeping, make up the practice of what is known in Tibetan Buddhism as dream yoga. In some lineages, dream yoga was reserved for those on a three year retreat and was only taught as part of the famous Six Yogas of Naropa. These days, however, some of the veils of secrecy have been lifted and allowed it to become a practice that allows dedicated practitioners to extend meditative awareness throughout sleep and liminal states, subsequently, throughout death and dying as well. Apparently, if we can truly master astral projection, then at the point of death, when our consciousness separates from the physical body, as believed in this tradition, we will be accustomed to this process and be able to guide it consciously, recognize the nature of mind, and reach full spiritual enlightenment, rather than kind of faint into unconsciousness. As the late great Tibetan master Akong Rinpoche once said, learning the basics of astral projection is good. At death, the same things happens, so it's good to practice. Essentially, for a seasoned astral projector, when death leads to the separation of consciousness from the body, it will not be their first rodeo. This idea of being able to consciously guide our death experience rests upon the concept of something called the "Bardo." The Bardo is a Tibetan Buddhist word that means place in between, and it's used to describe any transitional state of existence. Just as the dream is the bardo between falling asleep and waking up, life is the bardo between birth and death. However, usually when you hear the term, it refers to the after-death bardo which describes the intermediate states between death and rebirth. The after-death bardo state is said to be dreamlike in nature and our entry similar process to that of falling asleep. So it's believed that if we are able to fall asleep consciously and astral project, then we can use these skills in practices to die consciously and then recognize the dreamlike bardo lucidly, or, project our mind stream to a favorable rebirth, because the Tibetan Buddhist practice this to choose where they want to be reincarnated next, and also to receive teachings from masters that have passed on already. And, it's said that if practitioners can do this, then they can recognize the nature of their mind and have the potential to reach full spiritual awakening. Essentially, astral projection training can be used to prepare us for the bardo that we enter once we have left the body at the point of death. It is said that even if a yogi has practiced meditation for a whole lifetime and still hasn't attained full realization, he has one last shot at it: death. I want to tell you the story about Mindrolling Rinpoche. Mindrolling Rinpoche was an old Tibetan Buddhist lama, known for seeming to be asleep for the majority of his last years of his life. Why would he do this, spend these years sleeping? Because he knew that his body was dying, and so he knew that there was only one practice to focus on before death: astral projection. He spent most of his days sitting upright in meditation, but on the cusp of sleep, in that liminal space where entry into either a lucid dream or astral projection is easiest. This didn't stop students coming to receive his blessing, though, so his wife would briefly wake him up, and still half-asleep, he would give them a blessing and then go back into his dream yoga meditation. One day, he woke up suddenly and yelled to his wife to make tea for five people, before dropping back to sleep. Half an hour later, five travelers turned up at the door. Their Land Rover had broken down in the valley, and they had walked to his monastery for help. The story goes, he had astral projected out of his body, and he'd seen them walking up towards the monastery, so he wanted their tea ready for their arrival. Although we're probably not at his level yet, we can begin to think about death and our mortality and reap some of the benefits that comes with it. This is why we're going to do an exercise called "Things I Might Have Done Differently." And we're going to explore what we would do differently in our own life, if we knew that we were going to die. Just take a moment now to come into an awareness of your body and breath. You might like to close your eyes, and then just notice how you're breathing. Rise and fall of the chest, air coming in through the nose or out through the mouth, bringing your attention to the inhalations and exhalations, dropping into an awareness of the body, tuning into how you feel right now, accepting any feelings that might be there. And I'd like to invite you to imagine that you're on your death bed. Your mind is clear and you have no fear. A nurse you particularly like and who is kind is by your bedside. And she asks you, what things might you have done differently in your life? Take some time to consider this question, with no pressure to find an answer, just seeing if anything comes up. When trying to think of what we might do differently, it doesn't have to be big things, just real things, personal to you. Try to think of at least three things that you might have done differently. For example, spent more time with my friends, said "I love you" more, or been more generous with money maybe. What is it for you? Okay. Release the visualization now and remind yourself that as you're not on your death bed, you have the opportunity to actually do things differently from now on. Can you make a pledge to do those three things so that you can die without regret whenever death comes? If you feel that would be too challenging, try and at least do one. And whenever you're ready, open your eyes. Your actions for today: in your projection journal, write down the insights that came up for you during this exercise. Commit to doing at least one thing differently in your life moving forward. It might be scary, but you'll see how good it feels. And then maybe you'll find the courage to do the other two things as well. If you feel confident or comfortable, share that point with your tribe, what are you going to commit to. And as always, keep practicing the techniques and passing through the hypnagogic state consciously. Well done! Today was pretty tough. I'll see you tomorrow.

LESSON 25: Lift Off: Exit the Body With the Target Technique
--------------------
<v ->Hello, beloved travelers.</v> Get your bow and arrow ready because today, we are going to learn The Target Technique. This excellent method was invented by author Edward Peach, AKA Ophiel, who called it The Little System. Later, it was refined and reworked by several other authors. The idea is to exit the body by using active imagination and memory to pretend you're at a different location. As always, we do this when we are deep in the mind awake body asleep state. We tune into the energy body so that the shift becomes real and then we exit. We're going to learn how to do this today. Then you'll practice it tonight when you listen to the guided audio. Here's how to prepare. Step one, first, you pick out a target location. Usually it's a location that you're very familiar with. One popular location is your front door or your bathroom, maybe where you get ready in the morning. Step two, the next bit is to take three minutes to visit that location physically; go there for real in your physical body. When you're at your target location, keeping to your spot, I'd like you to investigate the space through your touch, your sight, your smell, and hearing. Use your hands or body to explore the space. What does it feel like? What does it look like? Bring your attention to the surfaces. What's the texture? Is it flat or smooth? Round or rigid? Does it feel cold or hot? Can you smell anything in the space? And what does the ground feel like beneath you? Notice what sound you can hear and what you can see surrounding your area. How far away are you from the wall or a chair or any item in the space that you can see? Commit this to your memory. What does the atmosphere feel like to you as you stand there? Focus all your senses on perceiving the space around you. Capture a detailed snapshot like a living photograph to your mind. For example, if my target location was my front door, I'd try to notice everything about it. The doorknob, the grooves, the features, the color, and the texture. Where does it connect to the floor? And what's above the door? What could be to the right side or the left? And I'd turn the doorknob and I'd feel its texture; is it cold or warm? How heavy is it when I open it? Does it make a swing ,or is there a creaking noise? Then I'd step inside, and I'd notice the surroundings in the hallway. Are there shoes on the door or is there coats hanging nearby? Is it dark or light? Maybe there are things in the hallway, pictures on the side. I'd close the door behind me, walk inside the house or apartment, and notice things that I pass by, decorations, photos, what do the walls look like? I'd saturate my memory as much as I can with all of these surrounding features, and I'd engage not only my sense of sight but also my other senses as well. Do this with your target technique. Then, get your room ready, so you're all settled to do a practice, and follow the guided audio. When you've done everything you can to create the best conditions, been to the toilet, chosen your position, got your cushions ready, then listen to the guided audio. This will take you into the mind awake body asleep state through to the Target Technique. During this process, I'll ask you to use your imagination to pretend that you're back at the target location. Let's use the door as an example again. Imagine you can see your front door as vividly as you can. Let's say it's your target and you're recalling it now. Remember what it looks like. Recall what you saw looking down at the door. Remember what it felt like to look to the right and to the left, and remember what the doorknob felt like, the colors and the grooves and the patterns, the textures; was it cold or warm? And then you turn the doorknob, and then you'd step inside. You'd look around and use your imagination to recall the objects, everything that you can remember, the entryway, shoes on the floor, coats hanging nearby, and in your imagination, you would reach out and touch the wall. Feel the textures; you'd sniff the air. Try to imagine the same smells as before. We're trying to create the same atmosphere by using our active imagination to walk through the target location exactly as you did when you were in the physical body. When we do this in the guided audio, convince yourself as much as possible that you're in your target location. When you do this for long enough, you might feel a sudden shift of awareness. You might find yourself suddenly at that target location and fully out of body. Alternatively, you might suddenly find yourself back at your body's location but in the vibrational state. If this happens, you can respond by following the vibrations, using your intuition, or you could switch to an exit technique such as the Rollout or Levitation or Sinking. It's okay to leave the Target Method if another exit technique feels right for you in the moment. There is that flexibility. Now, I want to stress that the target could be anything or anywhere. I just used the front door as an example, but you could easily use your target as your bathroom. If this was the case, you'd imagine the mirror or the toilet or the toothbrush, your soft towels, the cold tiles maybe, the floor, so on and so forth. Don't forget to start with somewhere familiar and nearby. This makes it easier to remember. Some people find it's much more effective to practice the Target Technique when they're away on holiday or on a trip or perhaps in a hotel bed. In other words, you're lying down on the hotel bed, and your Target Technique could be your home bedroom where you'd imagine you're looking back at your home and lying on your own bed surrounded by all your familiar things in your room, lamp, bedside table, blankets, a favorite pillow, and so forth. When you get better at it, you can then have a target that's far away, such as on a white sandy beach in Florida, or even further away, targets like the Pyramids in Egypt, maybe even a crater on the moon. Try to make it fun and see how realistic you can do this. Your actions for today: so your task is to practice the Target Technique following the three steps as laid out in this session. Go for a bullseye, and if you miss the mark, don't worry. It's your first time trying this. Just next time, move the target closer. Good luck.

LESSON 26: Test Your Projection Skills With a Group Experiment
--------------------
<v ->Welcome back, dear travelers.</v> Today, it's time to roll up your sleeves and put into action everything that you have learnt so far because we're about to do an experiment. I hope you are as excited as I am. Let's begin. Dr. Charles Tart studied a gifted astral traveler, Miss Z. One night in a laboratory, she was lying in bed. He was on the other side of the screen, and he'd set a five-digit random number high above her bed where she couldn't see it. Then when she awoke out of the altered state, she called out the correct five digit numbers in the right order. The odds of this are one in 100,000. He tried a similar experiment with Robert Monroe. Monroe didn't get the numbers, but he saw the laboratory technician talking to a strange man outside the building which later turned out to be true. Just like Monroe and Miss Z, we're going to test our projection skills with an experiment. Every Astral projector comes to a point where they want to know, "Am I just hallucinating or is astral projection real?" Of course, that depends on how you define reality. But what we usually want to know is am I seeing objective everyday reality? So we go through this phase where we try to get verification that what we see and experience is true. One actual projector who in an attempt to prove the reality flew down to the parking lot whilst he was out of body to find his own car. He soon realized that all the cars were white. So he concluded, "Oh, I must be hallucinating." Then when he went back to his body and looked outside, he discovered it had been snowing, and all the cars were indeed white. These little pieces of proof often seem to happen by accident. There also seems to be more success when there's an emotional bond involved such as with a friend or family member. When we try to prove it for ourselves, it's often a little bit hit and miss. Let me explain. I do experiments with my workshop participants. This one time I placed a specific object, one that I had a strong emotional connection to, on the top of my wardrobe. I gave consent for the participants to project into my room and verify what it was. The object was a purple cuddly toy named Ms.Lavender Rabbit who represented fertility and children to me. What I didn't tell them to make it even harder was that I'd moved house the day before the experiment. So not only did they not know where I live, but also I'd spent five years in my old house and only one night in my new one. So which one would they know to go to in the out-of-body state? There were some very curious hits. One student said, "I saw a glass rose holding up an egg." Another said, "I saw a rose quartz crystal shaped like an egg." A couple said there were children's toys on the floor and down the side of my bed. But another one saw something completely different. She said, "I see you near lockers with groups of kids." There were a few interesting things here. I have a rose quartz egg that looks like glass in my bedroom right next to my wardrobe on my meditation altar. So one person got that and almost another did, but it wasn't the object that I placed on top of my wardrobe, although it was linked to fertility. Also the theme of children kept coming up, which is what the rabbit represented. And lastly, in my wardrobe, I have a bag of t-shirts with street dance crews names on them. These are sentimental to me because I used to teach dance in schools and I'd call the groups my kids. I'd often be in the PE area where there were lockers, getting them ready for dance rehearsals. Did the projectors somehow pick up on the memory and emotion of the energy associated with those items as well as seeing them? This is why I think it's easier to evidence experiences with meaningful objects or symbols rather than letters or numbers. Not only is it easier to remember during the OBE itself, but often we tend to be more right-brained, and the language area of the brain is on the left side. So identifying shapes, colors, and concepts is a lot easier which is why I have hidden the perfect object just for you. But before I explain how to do the experiment, there are some things that you might like to know to try for yourself. When setting up observations like this, make sure to keep them simple and close distance, at least at first. Don't expect to travel to Hawaii and identify a refrigerator magnet on the 12th floor of an apartment building on the third street. Keep it close by. The reason is when we're out of body, we can get easily distracted by things. So, here are three tests that you can do for yourself. The playing card experiment. Author Robert Bruce suggests shuffling a deck of playing cards or tarot cards and then placing the deck on a shelf above your head and then flip the top card up so that it's only visible from up in the air. After you leave your body, go to look at the card and memorize it. When you get back to your body, look at the card and see if it matches what you saw in your OBE. The door number experiment. Find a door number or a car license plate from a street you haven't been down before. It's important it's a new place, otherwise skeptics can just say, "Well, you're drawing on memory and imagination." So it needs to be a place that you haven't seen or been to before. This is great to do whilst on holiday or traveling. Visiting your friend experiment. Ask your friend for consent to visit them around the time that you plan to do your experiments such as at the weekend. Go to their house, and see what they're up to. Then when you get back, report back to them what you saw and see if your experience matches up with what they were doing. If your friend is up for doing something a bit more scientific, you can give them five index cards and draw a symbol on each one, such as a yellow circle on the first, a red plus sign on the second, on the third draw blue wavy lines, on the fourth a box that's black, and on the last, a green star. Number them from one to five, and have your friend use the random number app on their phone to choose a card; have them set it somewhere you can easily travel to, then leave the body and try to identify the card. So these are some things that you could do in your own time. Your actions for today: our group experiment. Are you ready? Here's what we're going to do. I'm going to place an object on top of my wardrobe for you to find. I give you consent to enter my room to see what that object is. Tonight, you get ready, and set up for practice as usual. You then do the Wake Back To Bed technique. And during that, you do 10 minutes of meditation where you have full intention to successfully locate the object, then get back in bed and use the target technique which will be guided on the audio track to get into the mind awake body asleep state and do the target technique exercise. Don't forget to make the object on top of my wardrobe your main target, the place where you want to end up, the thing that you want to see last. Then when you return, write in your projection diary anything you saw or you felt or you sensed. Remember, information in the astral is not just visual. So write anything and everything down. You never know, that little thing that you thought was nothing could end up being an important part of the puzzle. I'll see you tomorrow when we'll find out what the mystery object is. Good luck. See you then.

LESSON 27: Landing Safely: Embodiment & Integration
--------------------
<v ->Hello, heroes.</v> How was the group experiment for you? Did you do it? Are you on the edge of your seat right now, dying to know what the answer is? Okay, so, the special object, the one I chose specifically for you that I placed at the top of my wardrobe, is the Magician card from the arcane tarot deck. This card means inspired action, new beginnings, limitless possibilities, and manifestation. The magician takes the seed of an idea and makes it happen. It is connected to new beginnings and new worlds. This card reminds me that we are truly magical beings and we can tap into that magic anytime, should we wish to. Did you see this in your OBE? Maybe you entered my room and literally saw the card on top of my wardrobe. Maybe you tapped into the energy, the symbolism of it, and felt those qualities that I just described. Or maybe you sensed stereotypical things linked with the magician, such as top hats, white rabbits, magic wands, or a similar figure, like a wizard or a witch. If you fell asleep or were pretty far off the mark, don't worry. Getting a bullseye on your first try is actually quite rare. After all, we are still honing our astral projection skills, but it's a fun way to put them into practice, so it was definitely worth the effort. Now, today's lesson is all about grounding and integrating everything that you've experienced in the astral planes to your everyday lives. And I'd like to open with a quote from Indian philosopher, Adi Shankaracharya, "Knowing that I am different from the body, I need not neglect the body. It is a vehicle I use with, to transact with the world. It is the temple that houses the pure self within." Coming home to our bodies and living in the here and now, in the human realm of which we were born into for a reason, is why integration and embodiment is a vital part of astral projection or any self-growth or spiritual practice. To process what you discover and then live and breathe your revelations in an authentic, heartfelt way, for it to evolve your consciousness and become a part of who you are, is how we bring it back down to earth and integrate what we've learnt. Otherwise, it's like attending school and not taking onboard the teachings. We're never going to graduate. And if we don't listen in class, we're going to have to keep attending the same lesson over and over again. And let's face it, life's short. No one's got time to waste. So how can we make the best of our experiences? Integration is about assimilating new information that your mind is now aware of with your body, heart, and soul, allowing this new level of awareness and flow of energy to move through us without resistance. Granted, if we've had a hard truth that we've learnt about ourselves or experienced wonders of the universe, it could be a pretty challenging process. You might have gained an insight or had an epiphany. Sometimes the realizations can be so subtle, so nuanced, that you may not know it tangibly, but you can feel that there's been a shift within you. These new findings may have a knock-on effect of emotion, from apprehension, or I'm not really sure what to do about this? And confusion, what does this mean? To excitement, wow, that was mind blowing, and even euphoria, this is going to change my life forever. This could result in having new decisions to make, a different career path to take, a solution to a problem leading from the heart. Or you might need to have that conversation with a loved one. Whatever surfaces for you as a result of your astral travel, it's absolutely paramount to process and integrate your experience. And let me tell you a secret about integration. Firstly, only you can integrate your experience. No one can do it for you. They can't tell you what you've experienced, because it's your experience. It's your truth. Secondly, how you make sense of your experience will largely determine how it influences your life. For example, let's say three people have the exact same astral journey. They visit a place, meet someone, and receive a message. One of them fixates on the place that they visited and decides they don't like it. It's bad news; it's negative. Another focuses on the encounter that they had and begins to live their life in alignment with the message that they were given. And the other is not really bothered either way. It didn't mean a lot. They just shrug off the experience. This same astral journey had the power to be incredibly detrimental or incredibly beneficial, depending on how the person made sense of it. So how we think about and understand our experiences is almost as important as the thing itself. Now, part of that example was true. One of my case studies, Justin, had a long astral journey. During it, he was given a message. This is what he said about his own experience: "I noticed this woman sitting to my right. Her appearance was a motherly figure, so I kind of guessed that this is the person I'm supposed to talk to. So I asked her, 'Is there anything I need to know?' She looked at me really closely. As she looked closer, she was glowing. And I kind of got the hint that, okay, this person is guidance; it's a message for me. She said, 'Do your best and the system will help you along.' And those words, they guide everything I do. It's probably one of the simplest bits of advice I've ever received, but also one of the most profound; that's how I've changed how I interact with everything and everyone around me. It even influenced my relationship with my daughter." Following through, by taking action, like Justin did, and mirroring your new awareness in an integral way on all levels of physical, mental, emotional, and spiritual plains is one of the best ways to bring our newfound wisdom into our lives. Here's one way how to do that, to really ground ourselves. In her autobiography, "A House with Four Rooms," English author Rumer Godden said, "There is an Indian proverb that says everyone is a house with four rooms, a physical, a mental, an emotional, and a spiritual room. Most of us tend to live in one room most of the time, but unless we go into every room every day, even if only to keep it aired, we are not a complete person." The four rooms, which make up our being are the emotional, physical, spiritual, and mental. If we walk into these rooms each day, not only is it good for our well-being, but it helps to ground, embody, and integrate any astral experience into our life. Here are some ways we can open the doors to these rooms and integrate our astral travel experiences. The emotional room, the feelings and the heart. This room is all about connecting with creative ways to process your emotional journey; whether that's through art, music, poetry, or sharing your astral story with a friend, it's about finding the space to express yourself and your feelings, whatever it might be. The mental room. This has to do with our thoughts in our head, our intelligence, our thinking. This is about finding space to download your thoughts, whether that's writing in your journal, your projection diary, or even writing a letter. Also, cultivating gratitude by making a note of the five things you're grateful for in your daily life can help. These are one of the ways you can process your thoughts. The spiritual room. Connection to self, other, the wider world, and whatever is divine for us. People connect to spirituality in different ways. It could be about being in nature, practicing meditation, saying mantras or prayers, doing a deity practice or going to church, but also about surrendering and asking for guidance, trusting and cultivating compassion. The physical room. This is all about touch and the body, anything physical. These are more earthly and sensory things, ways to ground you through the body. Things like eating, gardening, massage, sports, dance, or body work, immersion in water, such as swimming in the sea, or even having a bath. All the physical stuff that will allow you to connect to your body helps us to enter the physical room. When choosing what activities to do, you might like to think about what type of person you are. If you're someone who's quite driven and quite ambitious, it might be that you need to adopt a gentle approach over force. If you're the type of person who might hesitate, ruminate, and possibly even stagnate, it might be that you need to take action-oriented tasks. This is one of my favorites because it's also a great way to ground after returning from your astral travel. Tapping is based on the combined principles of ancient Chinese acupressure and modern psychology. It's like psychological acupressure, a self-treatment for settling emotions through using the body. Studies show that it decreases cortisol, the stress hormone, and it brings us back into our bodies.
